Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of these, one method is to make three or four cauteries, by tracing according to the length of the vein, and according to the shape of the cautery which we have described before; do not press your hand upon the cautery throughout its entire length, but let the patient lie on his back; another method of cautery is to heat the cautery which has two points, as we have demonstrated in the dislocation of the shoulder; lift up the skin where the vein lies, or where the pain comes from towards the left, and raise the skin according to the shape of the body, and let the cautery follow the contours of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Afterward, insert the two points until they penetrate the skin on the other side; then draw the cautery firmly, and in this way there will be four of them. If you wish, you can cauterize the entire cautery at three points.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the ulcer has healed for a long time, it is worth more than the other ulcers mentioned earlier.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	A cautery is not suitable for an epidenitis, except in the manner that is called "asclytes.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have described in sections, and your treatment does not help, then you should give the patient three cauteries around the armpit, one over the stomach, one over the liver, one over the groin, two on the lower back over the spine, and one on the buttock; the cautery should be close to the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After that, let the cautery remain open to ooze pus for a long time, and do not stop the treatment after the cautery; and healing will hasten, and the two intentions will come together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be the key that we have shown you before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what is shown there before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of foot swelling
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in a person with dropsy, and they are filled with yellow water, you should cauterize between the little toe and the ring finger on the top of the foot; lift your hand with the cautery without turning.Ande li sames piez que tu cauterizes entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, querre li sang qu’il vienne sus le piet, et adonques li piez sera desaloiez de la moistor qu’il contenoit; et si tu vois que li sang ne vienne mie sus le piet, adonques covient il que tu le cauterizes entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire en la plante dou piez.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go too deep, thus one will avoid the yellow awl, and let the cautery follow this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After do on the .ij. legs .ij. cauteries in each leg at the tip of the cuticle; and let the cautery be long, one below the knee in front and the other above, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries uncovered for a long time without curing, until the water comes out; then cure the others that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of menstruation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When there is an issue of the belly due to coldness and moisture, as the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are affected, and it cannot be cured by any means of treatment; and you see the patient suffering greatly with a strong constitution, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been spoken of before regarding the cautery of the stomach, using a circulating cautery; and four small cauteries around the belly, one subtle cautery on each hip, and two cauteries on the buttocks.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the shoulder, and one cautery on each elbow, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the large one, for the treatment is beneficial when there is good support.
de la cure des emorroydes	on the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are in the rectum, one or more, and are old and consist of large cold moist corruption, and are treated as described in the section on division, but are not helped by cautery: place III cauteries on the spine of the back, that which is entirely beneath the armpit, poking gently in a triangular shape, and II cauteries below the armpit; and if you think the stomach is chilled, and the meat does not digest, and one sees swelling in the face, then cauterize the face with a large cautery as described earlier, and another on the liver, and another on the kidney using all the cautery needle; and leave the cautery in place for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cleaning the wound until it heals.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the carnosity which is named "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you scrape the thelul, heat the cautery which looks like  .i. razor, and then put it all ablaze on the scraped thelul; and keep your hand so that the cauteries come to the source of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or .ij., and if there is a lot of thelul, cauterize each one as we have said. After curing with profiting ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the alchatim, it will have more help.
de plaie mal curee	of a badly cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, such a disease comes that it cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is a fistula, and it becomes suppurating and oozing corrupted moisture, then you must probe it with a thin rod, and be careful that you know how deep the rod goes into the tent.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	Then heat the cautery iron like a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the amount that the rod entered the tent, and repeat the cautery until the pus and corruption are burned up, once or twice or thrice, according to the amount of its need; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are nearby, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes into the bladder and the intestines, then be careful of those places, and do not make fire in fleshy places, and think that it is not dead tissue; afterwards clean the wound until it heals, and if the place is inflamed and the matter has been discharged for a long time, then know that the place is completely healed; and if the matter has not been discharged, know that the place is injured and the bone at the bottom is rotten; and thus as one of those whom we will speak of in their places.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes to the kidneys, and there are strong winds, and it does not go away, then you should cauterize the kidneys with a hot iron on both sides, as we have said before. If we cauterize in the middle, it will require three cauteries in a line, and they will be more effective.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the part above the bladder where the hairs of the pubic region begin, one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as the tip of a thumb; and he makes another cautery over the back, or two if you need it; and the cauteries should be curved as described before.
de la marris	of the mare
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the mare is cold and moist, and does not conceive, and the flowers are corrupted and their terms are delayed; and when they come, there is great pain: therefore one should make three cauteries around the womb, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries over the back; and the cauteries should be curved, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistors descend to the socket of the hip joint, and due to this it moves out of its place, and the sign is that one leg is longer than the other when measured together; and if the places of dislocation are discovered as hollow, then you must cauterize the patient on the hip socket with a .i. cautery resembling a circle, and mark around the socket as it turns, so that the socket is within the circle; and the cautery should be like those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not available to you, make .iij cauteries of the olive-sized great, and let the cautery be as deep as all the wounds; and heal it until it is better.
de la dolor de la hainche	of hip pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the disease is cured with what we have said in the section on cures, but the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purge the disease of the gross humors with stinking pills, or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After this he is cauterized; and there are two ways of cauterizing: namely, together with burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is done in many ways, one of which is as follows: you cauterize the hip bone with three triangular cauteries according to this shape, and make them deep and large, with an interval between each cautery the thickness of a thumb; the cauteries should be olive-shaped. Sometimes a cautery is made in the middle of the hip, from which there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you want, cauterize with the circular cautery that we mentioned earlier in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circles contain the entire hip, and all the thickness of the skin is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And that is the way they do it in sciatica when the pain is in the hip and does not reach the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it extends to the thigh and leg, they cauterize where the patient feels pain, and above the ankle joint four times on the left side a little; the cauteries should be curved, and burn through the thickness of the skin; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to one or two toes, they cauterize there where they feel pain in three or four places with what is called the "toes" cautery.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, do it more; and if he feels the pain below the knee towards the thigh, do cauterization with a knife or circular cautery, and be careful with all your cauterizations that you don't leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who had cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left it until the leg was completely swollen, and the foot as well, and it became pierced and all the feet were corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a stomach ache which caused his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two places together, do cautery in one and then the other, according to this method.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said about the cautery of the hip, whose method is as follows: make an iron that is as big at its tip as a finger nail, or a little less, and that it is wide between the teeth by the thickness of a thumb nail; and let the teeth be opposite each other in two parts, and also shaped like nuts, and let there be a handle of well-made iron; and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and dripping, and then put it on the box of the hip joint, and let it be turned to the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery and leave it for 3 days; and then make a plaster of butter, and let the wound remain open for a long time; after the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use this cautery sparingly because of its regard, and see little of those who employ it; and yet it is one of the good cauteries which can endure it, and where it occurs.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of medicine burns if you make the instrument to interlace in such a way that the edge of the door descends, and it is made of bronze or iron with one long side, and at the top it has two notches, and between each one there is the thickness of a fingernail; and they are open on the bottom and on top, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After that, place the box of the hip on the sick person lying on his sound side, and press your hand firmly on the box of the hip; then pour between the two circles of hot wax which has been heated in the fire for a moment, and let the sick person endure the heat and burning for an hour.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because there is biting as well as burning; and when the biting has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the hip with gentle wax, and leave it thus for three days, and apply butter until what is blackened by the scald is healed; and let it be for three days until suppuration stops; and that would be the last aid after the treatment of ointments until he is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the thigh or leg, then make the instrument that colors it according to what you did in the hip joint; and that is the way of the hot brand, and I wrote it in the treatise on the rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of each, and grind them together, and put them in a nine-pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Let there be a small hole in it so that the tip of a needle can enter; and put on top of this pot another well-plumbed pot, and put over the alkali and chalk a soft brand, as much as you have moistened your hand with; and let it stand thus until it descends to the bottom of the powdered pots, then take all that brand, and pour it over the chalk and over the alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then there will be much agony and it is relieved through various medical procedures and cauterizations of other limbs; for it does great harm like fire, and also by other medicines with which one cauterizes the hip joint, such as thistle and honey and soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells of a remedy by which a man was cured of sciatic pain and a vein in his hip, and he praises it highly, saying that nothing else was done to him, and that he was healed in one go after this treatment, and that he then bathed as instructed below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he describes how one should take green and dry litharge and grind it with a little fat, and apply it to the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is located, and leave it for three hours; by then the patient should no longer feel any burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then he enters the bath until his body is somewhat warmed, and he enters the bed, and the pain will go away completely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use such medicine with cautery unless after the evacuation of the body's fluids.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And دياسكوريدس says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it helps a lot; and the cautery must be done in such a way:
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take lamb's wool and grease it with old oil, and place it in the hollow between the big toe of the foot and the one next to it, which is called the 'foscile'.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After that, take dried goat's dung and place it in the fire until it becomes charcoal, then place it on the wool and leave it there until it burns out; do this again and keep doing it until you feel that it has reached the hip and the pain has stopped; this type of cautery is called 'goat cautery'.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes in the back, whether from falling or impact or from excessive evacuation, or from similar appearances of cold matter, none of these appearances are worth cauterizing for, except for that which comes from the diffusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary, after the patient has voided foul pills or other similar remedies, to make three lines marked with ink on the back, where the pain persists; and in each line, make 5 cauteries, or more according to the strength and amount that the patient can endure. The cauteries should be performed using the cautery instrument called "poins". If you see fit, make 3 or 4 cauteries with the medium-sized cautery instrument according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a stiff neck when they wake up, and fear; and you will find in the lower spine in the back and in us the appearance that comes over the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you cure it, then cauterize it with a silver cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the purple cautery evenly affects each part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery 2 or 3 lines apart, and have the points close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Afterwards, heal the site until it is healthy according to what we have said, and be careful not to apply cautery to any area that is swollen with pus and is affecting a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is caused by moistors that spread throughout the body's members, and when pain comes in the feet, which they properly call 'podagra', and when it is caused by a cold condition and cannot be cured by medicines, then it is cured by cautery in the following way: make the cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive oil according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a need to prick on the sole of the foot, do so with the entire cautery that one calls «point».
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this often happens, do cauterization on each knee with 3 or 4 cauteries of each part, using the entire olive-colored cautery; and if you need more, then do more, but do not hold your hand firmly for longer than the thickness of the heart is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery we have described in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make punctures around the wrist two lines; and if there is no pain left in the fingers, make punctures on each joint and on the palm of the hand; and if the pains come to the armpits or shoulders, cauterize each part, and use good treatment for the ailment and take medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good treatment and purge the phlegm, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	from the root of the eye socket
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a hernia occurs in the groin, and the testicles descend into the scrotum, this is new, so when you see it being cured, he must not eat that day. He should use things that loosen the belly so that the feces can exit his belly; after that, make him sit on his back between your hands, and order him to hold his breath until the testicles are healed, and bring them up to your fingers, and sign underneath the hernia on the bone of the groin, and all around a sign that looks like half a circle above the body; then heat up the cautery so it has this shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and dripping blood.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their place; and have him hold his hand so that it does not return; and work the thighs well for the patient, and put a pillow under his thighs, and the sergeant on top of the thighs, and the other on the foot which presses the hands; then put the cautery on the vein all over the palm of the hand, and hold it straight and do this until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the vein does not pop out when you are doing the cautery so that you do not burn him, and so that the patient does not die, or suffer some other ill.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And the cautery for children should be subtle according to the size of ears, and for large people also large according to their size; after three days dress the site of the cautery with butter until the scald is healed; then dress it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days so that the wound is well closed; and one should wait a long time before he starts to walk around so that the stitches do not come undone when he gets up to move about.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days when he wants to get up, have a well-made bandage ready for him, and wear it for another 40 days; and keep him in good rest, doing little work, and guard against too much eating and drinking, and shouting too loudly; and if he follows this instruction he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say hereafter about the treatment of cutting in his shoulder.
de la routure dou ventre	of stomach ulcers
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come in other stomachs and are known, and you see that they do not grow anymore, he should be cauterized with the fire cautery according to its quantity, and it should burn the third of the skin; after the treatment as we have said; and some of the ancients say that one should cauterize with a three-pointed cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first sign the site of entry and make a line along its width above the ulcer, and another across, and hold your hand still all over during the cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in a limb, either from falling or from injury, and that pain lasts a long time, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called 'sharp', and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb, its smallness and weakness, and its torture and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healed by the first cautery, that is good; if not, perform another cautery on it, for such is the custom that it should move in the member nearest to it, therefore you must apply cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Some diseases are aided by cautery with great benefit, especially those that arise from putrefied humours and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Now you have seen how to cauterize it, take care that the disease is in its early stages, and if it is cured according to what we have said above, and does not disappear or remain, but you doubt that corruption may spread throughout the body, then make five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the forehead, and two at the temples, one behind the ear, and one at the hairline; and hold your hand so that the cautery reaches to the bone, and so that the vapours of the gross humours may issue out, and cauterize the mouth according to what is described above.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	If the disease is scattered throughout the body, and it is clearly evident, then you must cauterize it with these cauteries that we have mentioned: one cautery on the head, two cauteries on the spine of the neck, six cauteries on the spine of the back, one large cautery on the groin, and one additional cautery on each hip; two cauteries on the elbows, two cauteries on the knees, one cautery on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; be careful not to burn the nerves that are on the back of the heel. Sometimes a cautery is applied to the bone of the wrist, and one to the bone of the stomach, and one to the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you do of cautery, the more it helps, and moves the profit; and know that the patient does not feel pain from cautery as the healthy person feels it, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cautery be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterwards, treat the site with a poultice of wheat flour with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes in any member and is cured by medicines and oils and poultices, and it is not healed, then make cauteries on the member according to the size of the member; and let the cautery be somewhat penetrating into the depth of the joint; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes cautery is done on the hand and foot and back, at the outlet of the nerve that paralyzes the limb, and thus if the swelling is removed; and yet no one should meddle with it unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the outlets of the nerves moving through the body.
de albaras	of albaras
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is awakened, and medicine does not help, then cauterize it with a moderately deep cautery according to the thickness of the vein, so that the whiteness is removed and its color changed; then treat it with a poultice of equal parts linseed and lentil flour, rose oil, and plantain leaves, as well as blood from the colon and almond blood. Mix everything together and apply it, binding it with a cloth and keeping it in place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of sores by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre appears at its beginning, and you see it stopping, then cauterize it with a cautery that looks like a circle, all around the perimeter of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet the wise say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; and yet I do not think this is good, for I have seen it happen many times that it is ulcerated and rotted, and a more certain thing is to cauterize around it, with a cautery called 'circle', as we have said about many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot subside
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it is slow to heal because of the excess fluid it produces, or because of the age of the disease when it becomes decrepit (that is, very old), and there is little blood, or because of time; and you see it getting worse: then cauterize it all over with many small cauteries, pricking as you go; afterwards leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	Because it will hasten its death.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all around with the cautery, then heat the cautery from which the form comes:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of the disease called  "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced the skin, and let the cauteries be such that the patient feels them throughout his body in such a way that the flow of the pus is relieved.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards, heal it perfectly.Si li saingne ne vult point curer ou si il demoure longuement en la meureir: adonques tu le remets a leu et covient que li fies 10 cauteres entor de l’esgoutte, et estraigne li keur par les eculz qui sont sus le piez, ou s’il ne veult point aler par les piés, adonques tu le traites a la maniere qu’adibele.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cautery by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease is called "corroding", and it is nothing other than a melting of the member, for it melts the members as fire melts dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can withstand fire cautery, then heat the cautery tools both small and large, according to what is appropriate for the location of the disease; after cauterizing it all over until you reach the healthy tissue underneath, so that nothing of the corruption remains, only that all that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for 3 days, and apply soft poultices with oil upon the cauterized places until the burns from the fire are healed, and all the corruption is removed.Et si li cauteres feuz ne puissent osteit toute la corruption, adonques covient qu’il soit remede par eschaudures de leus.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of inflammations caused by humidity.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after 3 days that a healthy hair does not grow, it is good; and if not, then restart the cautery on what is left of the corrupted hairs.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this hair loss is sometimes cured by medicine instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already described the cure for medicine ague in the division: take the amount you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of warts that come on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that on different feet a disease called "clos" according to our understanding occurs, and is a large, hard lump that affects the foot.Et si li pies sont trots, et ne peut aller en son office, que il soit eslongeant de la foyt que il doit; et si li pies de la main sunt trots, qu’il ne peut faire aucun ofis de main: et est li pies de la main et le pied trots, selonc la nassance.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this disease are according to two methods.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is, fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is where you heat the cautery iron as hot as a wax candle, and it is made of good iron to the size that it can cover the nail all around, and it has thin edges; after which you place it all around the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; then leave it thus for three days until pus begins to form; then make a poultice of crushed wild mallows with salt, and leave the poultice on overnight; then the nail will fall off and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound with an ointment until it is cured.Cautere d’aigue chaude si est que tu prends de l’aigue boullante et la mets sus li clou tant qu’il fieent giter, et le remuers tot entor, et le remuers tot entor; puis li fai un emplaustre come celuy del cautere de feu.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted away from the body, and often occur in hands and feet, then you must administer hot water cautery; and it is in this way: take a bronze or iron cane, or a pen of wattle, and place it on the nail and the wound, that is to say, warts; and place the cane so that it covers all around, then put a little hot water on it, and hold your hand steady, and press your hand as you turn so that the edge of the cane comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water deep into the root; and let the patient endure the burning of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will be uprooted at all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another, until you have pulled out all those in the body, then heal them with ointments that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the shaking treatment
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from coldness of the nerves, or from quartan fever or other [ailments], you should make four or five cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spinous process; and one cautery on the penis, and one on the stomach with an olive-oil cautery; this will stop the trembling and hasten the recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	There appear sometimes through the body sores or stinking pustules, which come from corrupt humours.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If necessary, when they first appear, one should make a cautery on the top of each pustule: with a thin stick of myrrh-wood, the end being taken in the fire, or a long root of aristoalogue, or with the lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning as they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow any further but the excess from which they come is destroyed and they are healed; but this must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	There are often great flowings of blood from the artery which is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cautery on the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stanch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to someone, you must quickly put your index finger over the wound of the vein, and hold it very firmly until the blood is quiet under your finger and no drops issue forth; then take a number of olive-oil cauteries, both large and small according to the wound and the location where the artery runs, and apply the cautery to that vein where you are holding your finger, and keep the cautery there until the bleeding is staunched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if the bleeding starts again when you lift your finger from the wound and the cautery goes out, then quickly take another of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after the other until the bleeding is staunched; and be careful that you do not harm the nerve nearby, and that no other ill comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well staunched by itself if the artery is large, unless by one of four methods we have described: by cautery, or by extraction if it is untreated, or by a strong ligature, or by medicines applied which have the power to staunch bleeding; and it should be bound and compressed skillfully.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	He who administers a tight bandage or places hot objects on top, or similar things, will not benefit much if at all.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and there is no medicine or healing available, then one should put their index finger on the wound as we have said, and press firmly on the wound and the vein; and they should not move it but moisten it with cold water often so that it becomes very cold until the blood congeals and swells and becomes firm; and they should make a splint in front of what is needed for cauterizations and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of wound treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all the diseases that require cauterization with fire or burning medicines, and their causes, instruments, forms of cauteries; and I have placed that chapter from the head to the foot, and I will continue in this chapter by the same way for what one can more easily find.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I may begin this, it is necessary, dear son, for you to learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and because of that greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I admonish you that you do not attempt foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For in many ways people come to cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from such who are so accustomed to their disease that they change easily because of the foolishness they find in their disease, and because of the greatness of its wickedness; and one must fear these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And from these there are those who give you their sense, and say: "Wait, I am healed"; and the disease is outrageous.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more confidence in your honor than in your desire, and do not open foolishly but wisely what you are certain of, and from which you can obtain profit and gain; and use prognostication and indication in the cure of your illnesses where salvation is turned to; and that will help you to this good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and uprightness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have assigned this chapter to you in discussing the topic of cautery, according to what has been presented before in the chapter on cautery from head to foot, so that you can find more easily whatever you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	You should know that this disease often comes to children during childbirth, and when the baby's head is squeezed too hard; and sometimes it comes from a relaxed cause that one does not know about.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	I have never seen this disease in adults; and of all those I have seen, death has always resulted; and for that reason, it seems best to me not to continue the treatment beyond a certain point.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and his head swelled every day until he could no longer bear it; and the moisture accumulated under the bone above the brain, between the heart and the bone. And if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, then you should make a large slit in the head, as long as two fingers, so that the moisture may flow out; and see the shape of the spatomile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the hollow is deeper, and the abscess is larger, then make two slits in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the openings of the head wider on each side, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand from within, and it does not close up again: then you must make three slits in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, draw out all moisture forcefully.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Afterwards, tighten the slits with bandages and powders, and put in wine and oil, and leave it thus for five days; then loosen it, and cure the wound by tenting and anointing, and let the head be extracted evenly, and give the patient dry food of meat from the pouch of moisture until the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you observe where the aperture of the abscess is, and the gathering of the pus; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut therefore where the abscess opens, and the gathering of the pus, and cut it according to what you can; and be careful not to cut the artery, and let blood flow, so that the patient dies from blood loss and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	from gout
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone that they have a disease called "cataract" in the eyes or the feet, and the disease is old, and the medicine does not help, then the last resort is cautery with which one will cut the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary, when you see them bend their heads, that the sick person bends his head backwards; then rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries are revealed, then press the neck of the sick person on the cloth; then look where the vein goes, and its path behind the ears, and it is very close to being repressed; then sign the paths inwards, then bandage both sides with an acute spatula, two parts at a time, so that the vein comes to the bone, and this should be done from the side of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, insert the spatulum under the artery and cut it from above, cutting also .ij. fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood will flow out continuously upward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the touch, then you must measure the amount of space of three fingers, then sign inwards and cut to the bone; and that which is necessary of blood put out is six parts, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone without any of the phlegm, then bandage so that no abscess comes, then press the wound and ligate it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	from the emetic
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old-age anemia comes, and catarrh is acute, due to moistors of the eyes and heat in the temples and ancient soddeness and similar things, and he has been treated by various methods of medicine and all of it does not help him, then we should open the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient should let the hair of his temples grow, and feel for the artery in his temple, because it opens well by its beating, and is not very swollen in some people who are too cold; and if it is swollen, then the patient should press on his neck with some folded cloth, then rub the area with some rough cloth, and anoint the area with warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatulum made of this material:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then lightly scorch the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it upward with tweezers, and carefully separate it from the tissues beneath in each part; and if the artery is thin, return it to the tip of the nail, then cup that part according to the quantity of the two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cupped, the blood will not flow everywhere throughout the body.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from 1/4 to 1/2 ounce, and if the artery is large, you should tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread so that pus will not come before the wound heals, and the blood will flow smoothly; then cut off the excess between the two ties in that same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with a hot-iron knife up to the bone until the joints are cut; and this is the best way, if the patient does not have a fever and is of a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery helps to end moisture; for this reason it is of greater help with moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the hole with old cotton and puts it on top of well-made tenting; and when they are removed, they are cured with dry medicines that cause scabs to form, and with tenting, until it is healed; and if without cutting into the artery as much as you work at it, you hurry to cover it with cautery, or you use vitriol and press it in your hand so that the blood is stopped; and if you don't have this present, put a finger on the spot so that the blood is frozen, and moisten the spot with cold water so that the blood stops, and press it as it should be; and what is best and easier in the extraction of an artery is that you cauterize the vein with this cutting cautery of 2 parts, but the cutter must be very thick to retain its heat for longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	Because when the instrument is too thin, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And between the two knives there should be a distance of one finger's width, and then when you have made an incision in both places, put the hot iron on it until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and keep the two heads apart because they are not welded together by this cautery; and this is how the cautery should be formed:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears are falling from the eyes that are above the testicle of the head, and medicine does not help the healing, and you see the face of the sick person turning red, and there is movement in the front as if it were trembling; and when the oil is thin and moist so that the hair of the eyelids has fallen out, and the eyelids are scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
