Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancient called it "cure contused", and it is that you do to the patient who has this disease, let him have hairs on his forehead, then make three slits in the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and one of the slits should be as long as two fingers all across the forehead going downward, and the other two at the two temples above the eyebrows, and beware of cutting the arteries that are at the two sides above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and each wound should be the quantity of three fingers across joined; and have ready a piece of sponge and cloth to wipe up the blood, then fill the spatulum with oil on both sides where there is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is to be made on the temple up to the second incision; and scorch all the skin between the .ij cuts as far down as the cheek bone, then make another cut from the middle incision up to the other second one, and then take out this spathanium.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put into the first cut the instrument that is called "culter", and is very sharp on one side and not sharp on the other, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the knife cutting towards the chest bone in the heart, and the other knife towards the bone, and cut it so that it comes to the middle split.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to what opens in the heart, and then make another incision in the middle split up to the other defiant; and then draw out blood evenly, and express the place for the taken blood; then put a tent of old cotton into each split, and put wet garments in wine and oil and garlic on top, and guard against hot abscesses coming; and at the third day loosen the ligature, and administer plenty of cold water, then cure it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other cures for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	from the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone has a sudden catarrh and you see the eyes are sunken and small, and the vision weakened, and the eyelids burnt, and the hair falling out, and pain in the head, and the patient sneezing; then know from these symptoms that this matter and these catarrhs come from many veins, and the cure for it is to let blood.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you should command the patient to raise his forehead, then make a large cut in the middle of the forehead, and another wide one nearby.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you should start the incision from the left temple to the right, reaching the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves in the temples that control movement, and when the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, and then insert old cotton between the two lips of the cut, and apply tenting with linen; then bind dampened cloth in wine and oil over it, and beware of hot abscesses; when it has healed, you should rub the bone until new tissue starts to grow, then treat it with astringent remedies that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat-flower and four parts of colophony, and make an ointment; then administer it in these wounds to promote healing throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the cleaning of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls from the ears is one of four things: grains, animals, minerals or similar objects like iron; seeds, such as peas, beans and lentils; or flowing substances like water, garlic and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it shrinks in the ear, or something else that doesn't adhere to or grow in the ear, put the ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, distil a little violet oil or oil of assafety, then bring about extraction; and let him sneeze from scent, and stuff the nostrils when sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and have the ear uppermost.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Frequently it comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, then bring about extraction with very thin pincers, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the forceps, that is good; if not, use a thin, small pair of tweezers made of soft iron and insert their tips into the ear canal firmly; then stop the area around the tips with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the forceps; then pull it out firmly. Often it will come out in this way, as we have said. If not, take a glottis (a pair of forceps) similar to those used for birds and insert an instrument designed for this purpose, then put some cotton around it; press the glottis against the object, whether it is a stone or something else, and pull out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it does not come out with these methods, you should split the ear so that pus and blood come out, causing a chalazion  and spasm; the splitting method is as follows: first, bleed the patient's head, then make him sit between your hands and turn his ear upward, then make a small incision at the root of the ear where the fat depends, and make the incision in the shape of a moon so that you can reach the stone; then extract it according to your ability, and suck it firmly with your mouth until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer .i. spatumile tenve subtle according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and bring about incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grains are moist due to moisture in the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with thin pincers and a suckling-cup, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	Therefore in the water that runs into the ear, the patient should use scent to cause sneezing first, and fill the ear with soft cotton.Quant il distend l’oreille si que li muque se distende, met a l’entree de l’oreille, es deux costez del garnement, quelque oile violete et suc, si com nos avons dit; et s’il ne peut venir fuer par ceste manier, si covient le faire estracter as pinceures subtilz.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on the affected ear itself.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out by itself, that is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If it does not jump out by itself, take many small stones according to the length of your middle finger and finger tips, and heat them in fire; then put one into the ear of the patient, and push on the other end from another part with a sharp stone upon the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this from stone to stone until all the fluid has come out, and so it will entirely jump out; and if you see that, take a straw and put one end into the ear, and heat the other end in fire until the finer straw is burnt; then do the same with other straws until all the fluid has come out, as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the insect, if it is of a small body, such as a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of a large body that can be felt, administer extraction with pincers; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the section on distillations, and if the treatment is not effective, then you should examine the ear in the sun; if any worms appear, pull them out with fine tweezers, and if none appear, take a sample of the fluid where the pain is located.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is tight below and loose above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Then insert the smallest end of the tube into the ear according to the amount of pain from the malady, then suck strongly on the tube; do this repeatedly until all the pus comes out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, then plug the tube with cotton as I have said for a stone; and if they do not come out as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven for worm-cutting, and you will find them in the section on distillations; and so distil your oils and medicines into the ear through this instrument, whose form is as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it can be made of silver or brass with small holes below and a wider opening above for distillation; and to press the distillation into the instrument use a well-made brass rod, and if you see fit, wrap cotton around the tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicines you use, into the rod, and let the rod be in the ear; then put the rasor, filled with cotton, into the ear, and press your hand gently so that the oil is distilled into the ear canal; and he feels the medicine inside, and let the distillation be a little warm, as one would heat it over fire to distil it into the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the cleaning of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without an earhole; and the same thing happens to adults due to the cleaning of a wound or a cyst inside the ear. This cleaning sometimes opens a perforation in the eardrum, which cannot be seen; and sometimes there is only a small defect, which can be seen clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when there is an opening that cannot be seen, it is a sign of a poor prognosis in many cases. In such cases, one should hold the affected ear towards the sun and examine it. If you can see the perforation clearly, then its appearance indicates the nature of the disease:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be narrow and sharp in front and behind, so that it does not pierce the ear. If the perforation is due to a cyst or body part in the ear, then one should hold it with fine tweezers and gently scrape away at it until all the foreign matter is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the growths are deep in the ear, take a thin, small razor and heat it slightly in the fire, then place it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you sense the patient hears poorly, pierce gently and be careful not to damage the ear nerves; then insert a tent into the ear according to the size of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, then take a tent and moisten it in rosewater, and powder over vitrialed vitriol; and if you see swelling in the ear, it is appropriate to draw out the tent and move another tent moistened with cerotum made of rosin oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then clean it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is bleeding, take a sponge and dip it in cold water, and apply it to the ear, and use other remedies which stop the bleeding that come from distilling treatments.
de la char des papieres	from the ash of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This treatment involves papers on the eyes when they are moist and dry; you should then extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the head of a spatula from its roots; then place powdered vitriol over the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it is without skin, one should cauterize it with a thin lens, and the cautery after the incision will help; and many times they return, as long as something remains in their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times there come on the ears things that look like gravel in shape and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "gout"; it is an assembly of thick moisture on top and bottom of the paper; the treatment is such: examine whether the gout is silent on one side and the other, and this is a simple thing to know; then they cut it open from the large part, then peel each part gently, then grab it with tweezers and crush it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot crush it without piercing the paper, then pierce it slightly, as long as it does not hurt the patient; and if the split is large, then stitch it up, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make any effort, for ointments will quickly restore and heal it.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstone is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then reverse the paper, and hold the hailstone with pincers, and press from both sides; and if the paper is removed by incision, it does not matter; and when the hailstone is crushed, wash the eye with salted water, and clean the place of that which causes pain until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is woven into the papers above it, and this happens more to children than to adults, and severely to themselves; and they get the catharsis in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes; and because of this they lie down on their faces, and sleep on them, and their papers are underneath their eyelids moistened by which the swelling and appearance have covered with exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place between your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of treatment is that the patient puts his head on yours; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains the exinah from each part, and then place it over him; and press with your fingers from both sides, so that the exinah is gathered within the circle. Then cut through the moisture with the spatulum, making a slit no larger than the wound made in the vein when opening it; and in some cases, the exinah comes out of the slit according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	So take a piece of cloth and hold it between your fingers and thumb, and turn your hand to the left and right until it is stretched; and be careful not to push into the fissure so that you do not go all the way to the sphenoid bone up to the eye, lest you damage it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exit does not open at the beginning of the fissure, then widen the fissure slightly so that it opens; then withdraw as we have said, then moisten a piece of cloth in vinegar and water, and apply it to the spot, and draw out with a bandage.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are men who grind salt and place it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal it until it is cured.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes to the place, then treat it with cooling poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hair from papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow from papers and are not of their nature, and they harm the eyes, causing various diseases such as tears, softness of the papers, and albuginea, leading to destruction of the eyes; the cure is according to four methods: through cauterization with fire, or with medicine water according to what comes before the chapter on cauterization, and it is done either by incision and stitching or with splints, according to what I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your lap, then hold the paper of the eye in your left hand; if it turns easily, that is good; if not, insert a needle with thread through the paper, either at the edge or where the hair is growing, and pass the thread over the entire paper, then hold it against the razor; next, cut into the skin under the paper, under the aberrant hairs, up to the great tear duct and down to the small one; then remove the thread and place a small tent of cotton and linen under the paper; mark a figure on the paper, like a holly leaf, but adjust the shape according to the amount you see the divided paper rising.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if to the one who needs it, one applies a large quantity of paper according to how the paper is moistened; then they make an incision along the two lines that you have marked, and they start from the larger nostril up to the smaller; and let one of the slits be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a hair root, then insert the needle into one of the two corners of the heart, then peel it all; then bring the two lips together with a single thread of fine woolen yarn through an eye needle, and draw out the blood, and allow the excess of the threads to dry over the two eyebrows if you see fit to do so; and if not, then don't worry about it, leave the stitches in for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitches using dry and constricting substances, because the paper sticks to the wound as it heals, but the stitches become loose (as the ancients say), and this is a job without fear; and there is another way: you mark the paper with a shape that is like the leaf of a myrtle, as we have described, with three pointed lobes according to the form that is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what is on top into small pieces evenly according to the shape that is there:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the wound is not equal, take a needle and thread, and sew it up in the middle; and sew another thread from the large earlobe, and the second thread from the small one, and bring the threads together between your fingers evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have sewn, as we have described, then bring together the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes the hair of the paper turns: so you must use what we said about the incision; but the sewing in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of bones is as follows: turn the paper and cut it inside according to what I have said, then make two bones by art, and two thin threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatulum; then tie two knots at each end where you hold the threads; then assemble them skillfully above what is on top of the paper of the eye, and pull out the two bones from their formed parts; and leave it for a few days, and the skin that was pulled will die, become numb, and fall off, as it heals.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it persists, and the wound has a large force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn, and the paper is raised, and the hair no longer hurts; and this is the shape of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the procedures are such that you pierce a thin needle and thread in it with a fine silk thread; then assemble the eyes and tie them skillfully, and let the length of the threads be about a palm long; then arrange another fine silk thread in the case and tie it at its end; then put the patient's head on your hand; and have it exposed to the sun so that the procedures are revealed, for this is a subtle and delicate procedure, then pierce the needle all the way through the paper until you draw it over the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the case, and thread that hair into the case, whether there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand back so that the hairs are drawn outward through the paper with the natural hair.

If the pustule is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then you shall treat the pustule from underneath to the very end that you have directed, until the pustule comes out from above the opening, and you see it with your eye; then you shall draw out the pustule and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair grows back in its place, and new skin forms over it; and if the hair is short, accompany one long hair from the eyebrows, and let them grow together until they are stretched out, and then cut them.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the eye pustule
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called "alacriaty" or warts comes in the eye, there are two ways it can happen: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or cutting, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way to treat it is to split the growth, separate its lips, and place within it tents of flax, and let it heal; and you must not use in its treatment anything that would dry it out and constrict it.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu. Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you must be careful that it does not heal according to its former shape; and these works which we have said are not remedies for this disease, but only to prevent it from returning to its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	from the pus that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is below and which is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Accidents come from wounds and incisions and cauterization and similar things; the way to treat them is that you take a needle with a double thread and pierce the flesh, and have it emerge at the left eyebrow so that the thread extends to both sides of the face; then the flesh above the needle is cut all the way to the broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that is good; if not, then take a razor and place it in the incision, and turn the paper over, and make two incisions along the side within the paper; and let the two corners of the incisions be at the two angles of the cut you have made, and form angles so that when they are joined together, the shape is like that of the letter "I" in Greek; then remove the flesh according to the amount that its sides are cut under the paper, then close up the two separated parts and sew them with a thread of wool; then treat it as we have said with softening medicines and poultices until it is healed.

And if the disease comes from a crack or a wound or cautery, then one should make a plain slit under the hair of the skin, and according to what is above; then draw between the two lips of a tent, as I have said; and one should perform the operation according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares machines with all his power how he makes the figure return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what he needs of operations and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Sudden movement of the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez. de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye

de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers. de l’issue de l’oil	of the exit of the eye:
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes open fully, and there is no disturbance to the eye or diminution, then you should ligature the patient; then let it heal, then put leeches or suckers without piercing, then apply a poultice of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla on the eye, then bandage it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the bandages is that you take soft bandages, doubling each one four times, then place them one upon the other according to the quantity that the eye needs; then tighten it from above with a firm bandage, and repeat the leeches without piercing to suck; then remove the leeches and leave the eye tight day and night, and if the ligature softens, you must tighten it much; then remove the ligature after the day and night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, then repeat the poultice, bandages, ligature, and leeches until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the rupture of a woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in a woven cloth, then it opens and comes out like a grain of resin, and is terrible to see; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you insert a needle into the root of the lower part up to the upper part, then insert another needle where there is a double thread of the upper arm; and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to its position; then pull on the place of the double thread and tie one part of the weave tightly, then pull out the needle and put a wet lamb's wool over the eye; and let it be until the threads cut through the weave, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the weave on each side of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes give a strong indication, he should pierce them with a sharp spatulum which comes from under the eye, and dry up the white moistness and draw down the eyes, and then let him enter immediately; then he should extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alkunnati" is not other than a tumor which has collected in the eye, resembling descending water, but it is not water; and the manner of its appearance is that you have the patient sit on a straight, prepared seat, then take his head in your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the tumor come out above your eyes; then it should be cured, and the light should descend and the patient should see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the tumor is not apparent as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you cause the patient to sit between your hands, then take the spatula and pierce the cornea with it slightly through the continuation of the conjunctive membrane with the cornea and the corona, until the pus issues; and when it has issued, drop into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek and honey have been boiled, and then let it be treated with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have discussed the appearance of abscesses in the division, and what must be done to pierce them; now act according to these instructions for the sake of health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should cause the patient to sit between your hands in front of light, away from the sun, and you should press the healthy eye firmly; then place the paper over the eye on your left hand if the eye is on the left, or on your right hand if it is on the right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is on the left, the instrument which is called "almagda", and vice versa if it is on the right; then place the point of the instrument next to the corona through the thickness of a hair in that white part of the eye where the tear duct emerges, and push the instrument called "almagda" skillfully, and turn your hand so that it pierces the white part of the eye, and you will feel that "almagda" has reached the hollow; and the depth of the channel of "almagda" should be equal to the thickness between the pupil and the edge of the iris; this is the corona of the eye; then you will see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the cornea, and then push the instrument down into the hollow, then express it under one channel after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water is coming out now, then the patient can see his own instrument and himself in front of him.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a while, if the water rises up again by the second passage, push it down with the instrument and when it is firmly stuck and no longer rising, gently extract the almagda by turning your hand a little; then put some gem-water in again and remove the eye from that.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then insert an eyeball soaked in rose oil and abundance of egg white, and bind it with clean eye-oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are from our time, put on comfrey crushed with an abundance of egg white.Et si li aigue ne descend pas la seconde voie, puis remette l’oil de l’autre costé, et met par defuer sus leu de l’eyelet une piece de lainne moillie en oile roset; et lie almain avec l’oil sain.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are some people whose eyes are too hard, then you should take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And if the water does not go down the second passage, then insert an eyeball on the other side, and put over it a piece of linen soaked in rose oil; and bind it gently with clean eye-oil.And therefore pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not cut too deep, but make the slit subtle, then insert the almagda as we have said; and at the end of the procedure prepare for the patient a suitable dark sleeping place, so that he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and keep him quiet from all movements, and give him light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and tie it according to its disposition for three days; then untie it in that same dark house, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then put the eye back in until the seventh day; and you must not do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but you should choose another time so that the water rises rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	if such a boil comes, you must unleash the eye before the seventh day, and receive from him who soothes boils; and when it is appeased, then loosen the eyelid and place over his face the upper eyelid to cover any eye, and let him be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then exit the house a little bit at a time, and return to his own bed; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the Land of Israel who told us that in his country they pierce with alum, and they suck out the fluid, but nonetheless I have never seen anyone do this in our land, nor have I ever read about it in books by the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagest, for those who do not know them can see them; and they are properly made of brass:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the ends of these be of the same subtlety, and the hindmost have four points.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart above the diaphragm
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes, strange, deformed children are born, some of whom look like scorpions with many feet; and there are some with a hollow back of a red color, and others with a smooth back of a good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	For those of these children who are smooth and not hollow-backed, you must make the patient sit in your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, and squeeze out any pus towards these children, and pull them hard; then cover what you can with a sharp, thin spatula on one side until you know that the pus is all gone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing which cannot be covered, open it with one of the subtle instruments lightly so that nothing remains; and if without it swells or an abscess forms, dry it as it should be; and if they are malignant abscesses, hasten to cauterize them until the pus is drained and all the corruption is removed, then pour on wine or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If it works and moisture reaches the palate, you know he is healthy; and if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, you know that there is pus in the bone above, which prevents instruments from cutting: therefore, you must insert a thread of linen, about the thickness of a finger, and tie it to your finger, with a knot between each finger, either one or two knots; then place the end of the thread into the nostril of the patient, as far as he can bear it, and pull it through the nose until it comes out of the mouth; children often do this in school, and it is easy for anyone who wants to do it. Then hold one end, which comes out of the nose, in one hand, and the other end, which comes out of the mouth, in the other hand, and pull them gently apart while holding the thread taut.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as much as you know that the nuts have corrupted this wood, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do so for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of the flesh; and then put into the nose a plug of cotton for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to cleanse the head, with which one distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and the conduit should also be made of the same material; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full for purging the nose; and it should have a handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart above the diaphragm
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises at the top of the diaphragm, and grows and becomes large, so that it is visible to the eye; therefore you should cut it at the beginning, and remove all of it, then place the cautery or burning medicine on top; and if one delays cutting until it has become large, then beware if it is hard, of dark color, and lacking in feeling: do not touch it with iron, for it is an ulcerated abscess, because when one cuts it once, great harm comes to the patient. And if the abscess is due only to pressure, not due to dark color, and you see that one can cut it all away, then evacuate the patient and cut it without fear, and clean the area of dry and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the heart is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when the solution of continuity comes in one of these cartilage openings, it is beneficial to some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this happens to someone, examine if the wound is fresh and contains all its blood; and then bring together the two lips with a stitch, and cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are torn on both sides, you should scrape all parts of their skin until they heal, then bring together the two lips with a stitch, and tighten it, and strew powdered dragon's blood and incense powder over it; and put an ointment of strong plaster or other binding ointment over the powders, and leave it to heal by itself, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of lip abscesses
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, there are hard abscesses within the lips, resembling grains of wheat, smaller and larger; therefore, you should turn the lips inside out, and slit them on each knob, and pinch and cut into each part; then apply crushed vitriol to the incision, until the blood is stanched; then use the leechwort, and cleanse the area of dry matter until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of gum swelling
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a growth arises on the gums, which the ancients call "albus"; you should hold it with tweezers, cut at its root, and let the blood or pus flow out; then place powdered vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders, over the site; if the growth returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it again and cauterize it; if it does not return after cauterization, and this often happens, then these are the forms of estrume for coping.
des sordens	of the eyes, and to the
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Some are clustered at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, and some are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, or green, so that the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; so you should have the patient sit in your lap, and open his mouth wide, and inspect the teeth where the sores appear, until nothing remains; and thus you should do for blackness, and yellowness, and other discoloration, until they are clean; and if one is removed at first, it is good; if not, then repeat it again the next day or the third, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth require various forms of estrume to remove them, according to what the work demonstrates, so that the rasors with which one scrapes the teeth have different forms from those with which one scrapes between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure a tooth of its pain that you delay pulling it as long as you can, because no one should do this; because it is a very high substance until there is no excuse to pull it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is compelled to pull, you must be certain of your teeth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain deceives the patient and believes it to be in the tooth, and forces the good tooth; and even though the pain is not relieved by this, until the evil tooth is extracted, for we have already attempted this with these saints; and when you are certain of your teeth, you must scrape around the tooth all around, spitting strongly to push back the gum from all sides; then remove it with your fingers or with fine tweezers little by little, until it is well loosened, then grip tightly with the tweezers; and let the head of the patient be between your knees, and hold him firmly so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Then extract the tooth firmly without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of these instruments and insert it into each side gently, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are pierced and loose, you should fill the holes with lint and gently constrict them with forceps so they don't break on extraction; you must work very gently around the gums to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful that you don't break it, or part of it remains, and the pain returns worse than before because of the root's sharp edge.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware of acting like ignorant surgeons who, in their haste and arrogance, sometimes break a tooth, or sometimes cause great illness due to the roots remaining, or the tooth breaking, as we have often seen. When a tooth is pulled, wash the socket with wine or garlic and vinegar; if bleeding ensues, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol; and if that doesn't work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, which make the teeth loose, have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth. These are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be made of large pieces so that they don't bend during pulling, and be made of good iron, and be serrated to hold the gums.
de la racine des dens	from the root of teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in place, you must put wet cotton on the area for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the area is softened, then insert the tweezers called "algefri", which make the shoulder look like a sore neck; and inside they are made like a file and that is their form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out with all these tweezers, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root and insert the instrument called 'althali', that is, forceps, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	Let it be sturdy and strong so as not to break, and if the root pops out through this, that is good; if not, then use all the instruments, of which the forms come below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And let one assist with this instrument which has .ij. tips, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools which are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tweezers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be outside so that it does not break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise master subtlety finds by himself his instrument, according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are many diseases in which the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their diversity; and if it does not break in the cart or the other bones, or it protrudes, then he seeks the instruments that he needs, which I have told you about, and helps with gestures, so here is its shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-fitting to hold the bone, so that it does not slip but can be held and removed; and then restore the site with appropriate medicines, and if there is a protuberance in the bone, and it is small, then cut it with all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to nature, and its shape is ugly, especially in young women, you should know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or ground down; then cut it, and if there is an air-bubble with the tooth, take this instrument, of which here is the shape, and it is like a small beak, and it should be made of iron with a sharp point:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the gum recedes little by little day by day because of the hardness of the tooth and so that you do not move the others; and if it is apparent that one can be filed down, then file it with a file such as this, according to its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file used to make needles; and file the tooth little by little day by day gently, so that it does not move until it fits; then smooth it at the end with a rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or distort speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth is loose:
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.
