When the tooth is loose, whether from a blow or from falling, and the patient cannot bite on anything without bleeding, and you have treated them with constricting medicines but it does not work; then they must be restrained with a gold wire, because silver wire turns green and rusts, but gold never moves; and the wire should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth inclining, take the wire and wrap it double between two healthy teeth, then place the loose tooth between the teeth with pliers, if there is one or more, until you reach bleeding at the healthy tooth on the other side; then restart the binding from where you began, straining your hand subtly and bleeding, until it does not move; and the ligature should be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cover the teeth with a thread using tweezers, and bring them together, and secure them between the healthy teeth, and place it so that it does not hurt the tongue; then leave it tightly in place as long as it can stay, and if it comes loose, or the thread breaks, then tighten it with another thread; let it remain, and serve in this way throughout its life, and this is the shape of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two rotten ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is reset in its place, little by little, as we have said; and no one who is not wise and experienced should attempt this, and sometimes the shape of a tooth from a cow's bone is made, and it is placed in the gap where the defect is, and it is held there as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the wound in the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligature occurs under the tongue due to nature, as people are born with it; or by accident from a wound that is stitched up; and the treatment is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and lay his head on your healthy shoulder, and hold his tongue; then cover the large nerve ligature so that the tongue is separated from its socket, and if there is hardening or growth due to a wound, then cut it with a pair of scissors and cover the ligature; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, lest you pierce the artery underneath; and when you have finished, wash the area with rosewater and garlic, or with cold water, then place a tent made of linen under the tongue; and tie the patient's tongue every night so that it does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, then apply powdered vitriol to the site; and if the blood congeals, then cauterize it with a lentigo cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it has turned purple or black, and the patient does not feel any pain, then do not touch it, as it is a chancre; and if it is inclined to become a blister, and there is moisture, then insert the needle, and open it with a thin spatumile, and release it from both sides; and if bleeding occurs due to your treatment, apply crushed vitriol until it stops, then return to your treatment until you draw out everything. Then rinse the area with rose water and salt water, and treat it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes ulcers called "godath" occur in the throat; and they are properly called almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take care: if they are hard abscesses of a small size and a light color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron; but let it be until it is dead, and then you will separate it, or it will burst by itself; and if it is of a white color and the root is thin, have prepared the instrument for covering, but first check that the abscess is calm and pacified.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit facing the sun, and his head be in your hand, and open his mouth and hold the instrument between your hands, and press the tongue underneath it, with which this is done; and let it be of silver or thin brass like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	As you press the tongue against this instrument, and see the abscess, take a needle and insert it into the tonsil, and pull it out above as hard as you can; and draw out some of the pus with it, then cover the instrument again, so that it is ready for use. It has a very sharp point, and the tip curves in one direction or another, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, cover it with tongs, of which the shape is like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And it is cut on one side, and named on the other; and when you have cut one of the glands, then cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and garlic, and if bleeding occurs, then gargle the patient with water, or with scorched pomegranate peels, or with bay leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses besides the two glands appear in the throat, so cut them then just as the two glands are cut.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and it had swollen almost closed throughout the throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passageway which was blocked, and she could not eat or drink, and would have died if it continued for one or two more days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had become so swollen that it had forced out two hairs from the nose holes.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened therefore, and pushed in the hook into one of the nostrils, then the abscess was torn open, and a large amount of pus came out; then I did the same in the other nostril hole, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I pushed the hook into the abscess, and scraped away some of it, and only a little blood came out; thus the passageway of the throat was cleared for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting at the abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, filling up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large; so I lanced it in the throat: thus it did not grow again; and I left those parts, and did not know what became of her afterwards.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When a tumor descends upon the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; but if it is thick and round beneath, it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it has been drained as we have said in the division, and the drainage does not help, and you see that the pus is abated, and it is thin, then you should cut it; but if it is round and not long, and it is blood-colored or dark-colored, then you should avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger in doing so.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it according to the manner that I have described, of its whiteness and length, you should cause the patient to sit facing the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, and draw it out from underneath, and cut it at one of the two instruments that I spoke of in the incision of the two almonds.Et li dis, qu’il ne bouge mie, si non que tu le presse a l’estrument quant il est fiche; car par la pression s’est a l’uve, et par la pression s’est a l’esgoutte, s’il plait a Dieux.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cover anything more than the excess that is beyond the natural term; for if you cover more, it weighs down the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two testicles, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear from covering, then you should use the cautery of the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is for acute fever.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of the cautery is as follows: The patient puts his head on your lap, and then presses his tongue against the instrument we have described in the chapter on cauterization, and breathes in hot air, not too thick or too clear; and uses the instrument thus:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has a handle at its head where the medicine is placed, like the handle of a spoon, and the instrument is pressed into the eye with all the medicine; and the patient lies on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from the mouth due to the medicine, so that it does not go down the throat and cause vomiting; then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it become numb and the stinging of the medicine is soothed. If you see something, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton on the eyelid, so that the cotton lies on the eye; do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry for four or five days. If you need to renew the cautery with medicine, do so, and after the cautery wash around the eye with cold water, and treat it with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this way, take calendula and hyssop and marjoram and rue and chamomile and avens and similar herbs, and mix them all or some of them into one pot, and add garlic, and let it boil. The pot should be well glazed with strong clay, and the pot has a handle shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it can be made of silver or bronze, and one of the ears is placed in the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the eye through the canal until the eye is mortified; then he should do this often until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the occurrence of a hot abscess, for many things can happen; nor do this beyond the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and place an egg white inside the tip so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; because the egg white will not let the vapor burden the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a fish bone or spine, or some other thing, becomes lodged in the throat; therefore you should try to remove whatever you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with the entire instrument, so that you can move the object; and if it does not reveal itself and is stuck in the throat, you should make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting. Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a dry piece of bread; and tie a string to the sponge, then swallow it; and when it reaches its destination, it will stick there, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of soft lead according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at the tip so that it can more easily enter the throat, and the tip should be lifted upward; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, or it may be torn, nor should you push the bone in; and move it so that the patient swallows the instrument, so that he can feel where the object is stuck; then he should swallow the instrument, or pull it out with the instrument, equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the medicine is blood, as I said in the division, through the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient towards the sun, then press his tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it out with a small hook or fine tweezers suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a curved cane and insert it into the throat of the patient, then heat the tip of the cane, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a fever all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Take a full glass of cold water and open the mouth and pour it in without swallowing, and move it around with their hand frequently; as soon as they feel the water, it will come out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then suffocate the patient with assafetida using the instrument I described for the fumarole of the throat; do this many times, as it will come out without causing any harm.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way to do the fumarole is to take a pot with burning charcoal and cover it with a perforated lid in the middle, and put the tip of the instrument into the hole; then pour your fumarole into it, and the patient should put their mouth onto the pipe, close their mouth so that no smoke escapes, but comes to their throat; and the blood will come out now, and if it does not, repeat the fumarole many times; and let the patient be thirsty, and eat salty and sour foods, and do not drink any water; and then they will need to go to the bathroom because of this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to draw out the blood is, when one can see it, like curved tweezers that can enter the throat; it is similar to a surgeon's forceps, and has roughness from lime, so that it can grasp firmly. See its shape here:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many kinds of abscess that appear, according to what the recollections that come later in this book from one and another, and they differ in puncturing and size; and there are two ways in which one is in its own likeness, and in what it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and the abscesses of fleshy places are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in action.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if one must not pierce abscesses as long as the bowels are calm according to their completion; and there are some that one should pierce when they become cruel, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	Because when abscesses develop near the joints and are left untreated until they are pus-filled, it is likely that the ligaments and nerves of the joint will become damaged, causing contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is near the principal limb and you delay piercing it until it has become pus-filled, it will harm the principal limb; if it is near the anus, it should be pierced so that it can drain, but only after digestion is complete, except for one that is near the anus, which must not be allowed to fester inside and lengthen, but should instead be drained immediately so that a fistula does not form and healing takes a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of the rupture of the abscess which is dead according to its completion, and that is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and from the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you must make the rupture in the most dependent part of the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the rupture be made in the longest part of the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and on nerves and arteries, and in all places equally where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	For those who bend, depending on the limb involved.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in fleshy places, it is better to wait until after digestion is complete before piercing them, as we have said.Et quant il est delez lou membre principal, et tu ne veillies le perforer tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, fuers que il soit meurez entor, si nuira au membre principel; et est grant dolur a celui qui le por; et li maux est plusors foiz perilluz.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before this, the body's veins will be torn, and it is full of filth; and perhaps the lips and its depths will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that should be punctured according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And one must treat small abscesses with small punctures, and large abscesses with large punctures and many slits according to the appearance of their size; and in such abscesses where it is necessary to split the skin, and cover; when it has become as soft as a dress, and is deadened, then one must do as they do with blisters: and there are some which are split into three angles, and some of which are covered just like a myrtle leaf, so are abscesses of the nails; and there are some where one makes a round incision, and other incisions, and similar covers.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, such as a superficial boil, you must pierce it plainly; and when the boil is large and has drawn up a great blister, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the blister in one hour, but some of it; then stop the boil until the next day, then draw out something again from it; do this several times, from great to small, until the blister is completely released; likewise if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman carrying child, or a small child, or an old decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pus sometimes jumps out with the release of the blister, and the patient might die without your realizing it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, handle this chapter with great caution; and when you have pierced your boil, wash the wound, and see if the wound of the boil is small; and if it is a plain cut, then apply bandages of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large boil with many openings, then you should place a tent in each opening so that they press against one another; and if you have cut into the boil in part, and the skin around it has been cut, then you should fill it with dry cotton or rags of unbleached linen without moisture, and leave it for three days; then remove it and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, bring cold water and ease, and wet the cloth, and place it over the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply treatment and care, and the powders I mentioned earlier in this book; and if it is in the winter, and the area is very nervous, then you should place wet tents and cloths soaked in warm wine and oil over it; and if it's in the summer, and the area is fleshy, then you should place wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or cold wine and oil, for a third of the day, as we have said; then release the abscess, wash and treat it, as appropriate, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And now you should know generally about the treatment of abscesses; I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter on it.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	From the head come small abscesses, and they are caused by people who wear hats, just as the ears of a chicken are, and there are many variations of this type.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fat and smooth where there is moisture as well as pulp; and there are some that are hard and stony in texture, and there is no doubt if the artery does not make them contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the body is that you should test with every instrument called "trocar", whose form comes afterwards, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they open it from above and draw out the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, they scorch without leaving anything behind of the membrane that contains the moisture, for it returns again if anything is left behind; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply this to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who are left overnight will be cured.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then resume the cotton, as before, on the second and third days, until you know well that it does not stay through the night; then heal the wound with ointment that is appropriate, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess contains pus, cut it open along its length; and gouge out your eyes, and scrape off all the scabs, and put all your treatment on drawing out the pus under the skin; and if the artery does not respond, then do what I told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this for a stone-abscess, cutting and treating it as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the stone-abscess is lighter, because they are full of blood.Et si li artere ne fuit pas, si mettés li chié sus li berlingot, et li muesche a li costez, et li sienge au bout de la verge, et li vachez a l’autre cap; et prendes une fiole d’or et une de verre, et le piez ou il gist, et mettes li cief sus li berlingot, et le corps sus li piez, et les piés sus li sienge, et li col sus li vachez.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there is no moisture in any of these abscesses, either on the head or elsewhere, then I have seen such abscesses on the head of an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if anyone had cut it open, they would have made a wound just like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	For other abscesses that come on the head, except for those that come on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should be in the most dependent part, so that the pus can flow out; and treat them as they ought to be treated.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times abscesses come on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes elsewhere in the body, and they are large, and some are connected to each other.And these that come on the head, and those that come on children, if they have no moisture, and are not broken open, then they are called 'stone-abscesses'. And they cause great pain, and often kill the patient, and sometimes they can be found in the neck, armpit, groin, or elsewhere in the body. They are large and hard like a stone, and if cut open they will bleed profusely just like a wound from a stone.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And every scrofula is properly within its coat, as the nodule and abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similar scrofulae.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that are malignant and will not respond to treatment.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Therefore, if you see one that is of a good disposition for cauterization, and resembles the color of the body, and is soft in every part, and not adherent to the nerves of the neck or artery or duct, and is not deep; then you should cut it from above, and scrape away each part, and have the two lips of the wound cut back, if necessary, as we have said for abscesses of the head; and draw out a little at a time, being careful not to cut any nerve or vein, and not using forceps or knives that might cause the hand to slip, and do not go too deep, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put ground glass in the wound, or some powder that stops bleeding, and press on the wound; and leave it until the abscess is eased, and the wound softens, and begins to fester.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the bleeding is stopped, return to your work, until you complete it; then look with your finger for any small scabs, and cut them out and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the ulcer, you should not cut the ulcer at its root, but tie it off with a strong double thread, and let it fall without harm; then dress the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the whole ulcer, you should bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, so that no excess remains due to the size of the ulcer.Et si tu troves en la plaie grant quantite de sangue qu’il ne se peut estaincher a ton ovraige, si covient que tu metes li sur la plaie un panne, et le tiens fort; puis emporte li sang, et laisse li panne adessuz tant qu’il soit estanchié.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	then you must understand how to cover the root of it, and pull it out, and cut it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulae that have a superfluity, pierce where it shows pus; and pierce in the same way as the one mentioned before, depending on it, then treat it with tenting along with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what is left of the corruption; and when the wound is clean, then treat it with an ointment binding flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	from squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is a written record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squint, the flap of skin in the throat known as the "epiglottis" should be cut; and this is done to aid them, because all the veins and the pormon are affected by the illness in those who have a hot abscess in their mouth, or in their throat or in both testicles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the pormon, one must cover the epiglottis to avoid loss of life due to strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to split the epiglottis, we should split it below III circles or IV a little split across, between the II circles or by the quantity of the split in the hyoid bone, not at all in the cartilage; and those places which are suitable for the splitting of the epiglottis so that there is no flesh in it, and the vessels are long from there.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the throat all the way to the Adam's apple, then split the windpipe until it reaches the voice box; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then cut the larynx, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe of the voice box which jumps out through the hole that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed that we doubt strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound from the heart, and sew it up entirely without the cartilage; then administer medicines which promote flesh growth, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged to be near death, and the deficiency of blood has been restored.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot choke, and he can breathe through the wound, and thus is guarded from death; and therefore the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the fury of the disease had passed, and it passes in 3 or 4 days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a maiden take a knife and thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the muscles of her neck; and I was called to heal her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found that blood had come out of it, and that she had not coughed up any phlegm or spittle except what came out through her throat, and the wind was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and stitched the wound and healed her until she was healed; and the maiden had nothing but a hoarse voice, and returned afterwards to her natural state; therefore I say that one should have no fear in cutting the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This hernia of the throat is called a "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of yolk, and it is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: naturally, and accidentally; in the natural way there is no danger.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident occurs in two ways, one of which is similar to a cyst, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is danger in it, and one should not operate with force unless it is small, and test and examine throughout the entire orifice: if you find it like a cyst, and it cannot be removed by any means, cut it as one cuts a cyst, and treat it to the full extent of its depth; examine thoroughly, and cure it as it should be cured.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways of doing this, all of which I will describe, and now I must explain the difference between a cut and a dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an issue is a fever and chills while the eruption has not yet passed and the rash is complete; then the fever and chills cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a cut there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a boil, and becomes swollen; and they are according to two appearances, either dry or moist, and very colorful, as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You should, when you come to the treatment of the nose, test and examine it first with all the instruments called "endoscopic", according to what its shape will allow in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of inquiring into abscesses is that you press on the most moist part that you find in the abscess, and twist your fingers gently, until you feel that the pus has broken through the skin, then it depends on the size of the abscess; then extract the instrument, and be careful about what comes out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moisture runs quickly, whatever its color, treat it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after an incision no moisture comes out, know that it is fat, so cut it in a cross pattern and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape each side, and guard the skin where it lies, drawing it healthy with the nail; and if you cannot draw it healthy, then draw it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing remains, it will return to the nose many times; and if a little remains, and the pain troubles you, then employ the wound with some corrosive powders, and tighten the wound, and place soothing hot abscess remedies on it, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the nose is large, then cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it as one who has a pus-filled sore.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the wound is bleeding profusely, and it is contrary to you or another, then quickly apply ground vitriol, and leave it for two days or three until the wound festered and stop the bleeding; then return to covering what has been left exposed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the probing instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three types of points, which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb"; and there are also three kinds: large, medium, and small, to probe abscesses of fistulas; and they are like the needles with which sorcerers are pierced, made from brass, iron, or silver, and those that are yellow prove more effective than black lead in probing the sinuses of fistulas; and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the opening.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the probes are very similar, as you can see: large, medium, and small; and there are probes with two curves of three kinds as well; and there are probes with three curves, and they are also of three kinds; and there are probes with two curves, and probes with only one curve, and they too are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their respective places.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these tools are sharp, and there are some that do not cut further than one side, which is used to scrape the teeth, so as not to pierce the vein or nerve. These instruments have handles with hooks, so that the patient does not bleed to death when opening an abscess; they come in three sizes: large, small, and medium, as you can see. They are only used on fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar areas; sometimes a small instrument resembling a finger is also made, according to this form, with which blood is staunched.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed in the area that heals by stopping the flow of blood from the veins and arteries, and sometimes they are cut according to this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell up when they become infected, so that they look like women's breasts; they remain ugly and swollen, and if one wants to cure them, they must be treated according to this formula from line .b to .g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scorch the fat, and fill the wound with medicine, then stitch together the two lips of the wound, and treat it until it is healed; and if the nipple sags downward, and becomes soft because of its size as happens to women, then make two similar incisions above it; so that one is attached to the other at the end of each, in such a way that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from letter .b. to letter .g.; then scorch the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and treat it with what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient will not rest, or due to bleeding, then you should fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it dissolves the remaining flesh and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpit
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	This abscess that comes under the armpit is like a hard scrofula, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus inside the abscess has been drained, employ the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat it with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like scrofula, they should proceed as we have said in the treatment of scrofula, and if the wound becomes pus-filled, they should apply cauterization as we have described earlier.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is exposed and the skin above it is swollen, there often occur abscesses; and so too with the vein, it becomes swollen and abscessed. One can tell which it is by its appearance: if it is an artery, the abscess will be long and deep; and when you touch it with your fingers, you feel a pulsation. And when it is a vein, there is a deflation evident around it. It is foolish to cover up this kind of abscess, especially when it occurs under the armpits, or on the arms, neck, or in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore one should avoid cauterizing with iron, and if there is an abscess on the head, it should also be avoided; and with one that is due to vein inflammation, cut through the skin from above down to the long artery; then open the artery widely at the edges, and separate it from the veins, so that it is exposed; then insert a needle under the artery, and pierce it all the way through to the other side, and bind the artery with a double thread in two places, according to how I taught you for the extraction of the two temporal arteries; then pierce the spot between the two threads with an introducer, so that the blood flows out from within, and release the abscess. Then administer treatment with warm bowels, until the thread slips down; then cure it with suitable ointments, until it is healed. And if the abscess is due to vein incisions, you should dye your hand with something taken from the abscess all over the skin, then insert a needle under the spot that you hold in your hand, and pierce it through, and put a double thread through it, so that you draw it through to the other side; then tie the abscess as I have told you, at one of the two ends of the thread. And if you are afraid that the thread will slip out, insert another needle all the way through the thread under the whole abscess at the incision of the first needle, and bind the thread in four places; then lance the abscess so that the superfluity flows out, then lance the superfluity of the skin and leave what is tied; then put a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil over it, then administer treatments with poultices and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, as abscesses come in the artery and vein, they come to the nerves when they are hurt, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and elbows and all over where there are joints, and it is a painful abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in various conditions without pain; and when one presses on it properly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body but under the skin; and it hurts all over, and does not move forward or backward, nor down nor up, and that which is in joints should not be covered by iron: otherwise there might be contraction; and that which is on the head or forehead, treat with a plaster.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, grasp it with tweezers and pull out the root; but if it is large, slit it with a blade, then scrape away the pus, remove the bone, and close the wound by sewing it up, then heal it.
des grosses boces pendans	large bumps hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the abdomen and nowhere else; it is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to ears, with thin roots and thick leaves. There are both small and very large ones; I saw a man who had two on his stomach that looked more like fungi than anything else, with no difference between them, white in color, with fine roots, and split open, from which moisture flowed.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them open and found one weighing 18 ounces and the other 6 ounces; the treatment for this is to incise if the disease is moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist with fine roots; then use a wide spathe, and have at hand the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when cutting there are often excessive blood losses, and if the blood runs out, then quickly use the cautery; and if you see the patient terrified and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-prepared thread and tie the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; then restrain it, and do not stop compressing with the thread until it cuts the joint, and the pieces come off without effort; and if the roots are large, then there is fear of cutting into the abdomen, but you can cut half of it, then cauterize it so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and beware of cutting the skin which is of a dull color and lacking in sensation and resembling milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is a deep abscess, and I will come to the treatment of sores next.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil bursts
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterization of a wound or from an ulcer in the syphilis, and is on the belly and in some of the bowels, as happens in other routs, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from wind; and if it is from the rout of syphilis and from the outlet of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a minor thing without pain, and it opens from various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is through the outlet of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with their fingers, it recoils, and then returns, and sometimes it becomes serrated, and grows larger at the entrance of the bath and from great exertion.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a minor thing, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, and it does not constrain; and if it is due to blood, then the abscesses open through these signs of large and hard boils, and they are stuck according to a certain quantity; and if it is due to wind, then there is a whistling sound when touched, and the action is such that you should look to see if the appearance is due to blood from an artery or vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Let the wound heal.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is in the intestine or bowels, then you must instruct the patient to tighten his belt and lie stretched out straight; then sign all around the swelling, and then command him to lie still between your hands while you go around the area you have marked for the spasm; then stretch the abscess open at the top halfway down the nail, and tie it tightly with a strong thread or cord of strong silk; then work the other half of the abscess stretched out over the string, and push your finger into the intestine; if you find it caught by the string, untie it and push the intestine back inside the belly; and if you find the bowels, take hold of them at the nail and cut away the excess; and if the artery or vein is causing problems, go about your work and take two needles and thread two strong threads through them; then pierce what you have marked with a cross as though you were piercing it, and stretch the abscess open in four places over the needles; then, when you see it, remove the needles and let the wound heal on its own, and scrape away the dead flesh; if it is thin and healing, then clean it and dress it as needed; draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound as appropriate and close it up.
dou chancre	from cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in the division the similarities of cancer, and how one should work with medicine, and how one should avoid the cure of iron; and they say that ancient people believed that when cancer is in a place where one can scrape it, like cancer which is in breasts, and in the thigh, and in similar places, one must completely remove it when it is in its beginning stages. And when it is old and large, one should not approach it, for I have never been able to heal any of them; nor has anyone ever healed any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatments, when it is in a place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile; then let them fester if there is a sign of fullness, then open the wound . Then cut off the cancer, and the hair from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow out freely, and squeeze the wound with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding from the artery or vein makes you feel uncomfortable, cauterize it until the blood vessels are closed; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
