Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hurry to pierce, but let the pain subside; and then have the patient sit on a chair, with two small seats for him to lean on, and support his back and raise his feet to the sides, apart from the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good ligature; then suck the wound towards the right side, and administer the instrument used to open the wound, from which the form comes afterwards; you must insert the rod first to know the depth of the wound, so that what enters with the instrument does not go in deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; if the instrument is larger, cover the depth of the wound with cloth so that the instrument does not cause discomfort; and let him hold the spout of the instrument upwards, and suck.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and one makes it on the soft hand, then it should be covered with a bandage, or with a sponge moistened in rose oil; and when the bowels are emptied, then you should put into the wound tents moistened in oil of red roses, or in dry green oil; and place the tent beyond the wound at the bottom of the injury, and place a poultice over the injury and over the little finger, with a clean sponge moistened in water or malvas flowers that have been cooked; then cure it after two days of ointment application, until it is healed; and sometimes raise the injury and the wound by an enema of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lilies and aristolochia that have been cooked for a long time; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is sunken in the injury, then you should beware of cooking with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is important for the midwife to recognize the natural signs of childbirth and the associated symptoms. When you see a woman struggling to push her baby down, and she craves the scent of rose, then the baby is eager to be born. This indicates that the childbirth follows its natural course, with the baby's head emerging first, followed by the afterbirth; and when you see these signs, gently press her belly to speed up the process and ensure a swift delivery. For when the baby descends, the afterbirth follows suit, and the mother's body is cleansed of any excess fluids through proper purification rituals. Any other method of childbirth is not considered natural.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Because sometimes the baby may emerge feet first, or it may come out of the chest, hands, or abdomen; and in some cases, it may get stuck in the neck or other areas, leading to dangerous complications. Thus, a midwife must be wise and skilled in these matters, guarding against mistakes and disappointments. I will now describe all the various scenarios and how to assist in each case.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child is born naturally upon its head, and the woman gives birth with great difficulty and her strength wanes, then make her sit upon a stool or have women support her; and heat some olive oil or fried fenugreek, and then pour it between the midwife's fingers into the small opening of which there is now the shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the afterbirth, and press on its nail until the moisture that is within flows out; and squeeze the womb of the woman so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then the woman should be enema with a mixture of fenugreek with oil of sweet fennel; then make her press and sneeze from pungent substances, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: then the child will come out now.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out, then you should gently reset them little by little; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on the seat, and lift her feet upward; then stand the seat upon the ground, and support the woman so that she does not strain while standing; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then press the hands with the nail which is described above, and extract the child, and reset in the same way.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the child's issue upon its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out onto its feet, it should be pushed upwards; then rock it back and forth gently until it is calm; then hold one foot and stretch it gently.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it leaps just to the knees, instruct it to grab hold, and cause it to sneeze with your breath; if it leaps out, so be it by God's will.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he cannot jump as we have said, then turn him little by little until he is in his natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then he is easily cured.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, take myrrh and oil of sixment and gum dissolved, and grind everything in the mortar; and apply this ointment to the woman's womb, then let her sit in warm water up to her ribs; and when she is soft below, make her a collar of myrrh and put it on her, and leave it for an hour; then let her sit on a chair, then cause her to sneeze and squeeze her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the child will come out now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	for the child to come out over his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, then the midwife puts her hands on it little by little; then she lies on her back, and the child hangs down below her feet, and she lies on her side in bed; and she bends her hands little by little, and then presses her hands on her belly, and pulls up the cushions from underneath, until the child is turned downward; and if the child does not cry out, then take its feet and move it about, then move its belly upward, then put your hands in; and rock the child little by little; and command the woman to hold on until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child which comes out width a hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I want to engineer the return of the hand: if it cannot be returned, then make the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her sit on the bed, and raise her legs straight up; then administer the mustard poultice that I have described; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a chair, then study how to return the hand; and rock the child according to its natural shape, and make her sneeze, and command her to hold on until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the child's exit at its neck, and spread his hands, and turned his face towards his mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I want the patient to dye their hand, then turn it little by little and gently wiggle their fingers; and when they are even, put on a poultice of honey and oil, as we have said, then instruct them to move their fingers little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and instruct her to grip something; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way with all the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this way all over the body, then scrape off the scabs at your fingernails, so that the moisture is drained; and if the baby can put its face and neck through her breasts, so that they are not restricted, and the baby dies, then bottle-feed the child, as you have placed it, and instruct the woman to grip something a few times; then release her gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the exit of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	They are strange things, and do not live, unless by name; I know that they are multiplied, and are separated by the caustic which divides them, which is bound to the bud; and sometimes they emerge as naturally as a tooth, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge painfully, then the treatment as we have said, and let the surgeon be skillful, and quickly and lightly do what he does; and act thus as is best for salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the sea one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and are all shaped like a child according to the measurement of the glorious Sage, and it behooves the surgeon to know all this, for perhaps similar things may happen to him; so act according as is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman after childbirth, as I have said in the previous section, and there is no progress, forcing you to use manual pressure, then you should check if the woman is of sound health and has no fear of death. Then, the woman should be laid on her back with her head tilted down and her legs raised. The midwife should apply a poultice made from equal parts of altheae, fenugreek, and flaxseed to the mouth of the womb, then grease the midwife's hands with these oils and poultices, and gently insert them into the woman. She should be cautious if the child is about to descend onto its head; insert the fingers into her vagina or anus or in her throat or under her tongue or below her beard or in her armpit or near her ribs. If the child is descending feet first, insert the fingers into the perineum and press gently on the sides of the pelvis. The midwife should hold the poultice in her right hand and place the bandage between her left thumb and forefinger, then gently apply it to the entire hand and insert the poultice into one of the places mentioned above until it reaches the empty space. This is how the poultice should be applied:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then file against the other nail, or the third if you need it, so that the extraction is even; and then press them evenly by moving from side to side, for movement to exit, and let the nails bite to hold the movement, as is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, then anoint the nail with some of its oil, and push it into that part, and pull the other part; and if nothing remains, then put this nail or a higher one, and do this until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and he cannot pull back due to the tightness, then you must wrap it with a cloth, as much as possible; then press on the fold at the plant or the ankle, and so you must do in the other hand, and in the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and it is constricted in its passage, or if there is a great accumulation of fluid at the top, you should insert the spathumile between your fingers, puncture the head, and drain off the fluid; or use the instrument called "almidach", with which the shape of the instrument that comes next in this chapter is made. And in the same way, if the child has a large natural head, draw out the bones with tongs, and if the head is forced out and strained by force, it will be split open so that the moisture that is at the bottom of the passage can escape; and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces as far as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, pierce it so that the moisture flows out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on their feet, the pull is light, and the movement towards the mouth of the wound is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If it is caught in the belly or the foot, you should pull it out with a cloth wrapped around the hand; and cut into the belly or the foot until the moisture that is inside flows out; and if other members are stuck, and the bowels remain, he puts his hand into the depth of the wound and pulls it up to the mouth of the wound; then he pushes in one or two fingers, and pulls it out; and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has formed there, one should not work on it, but rather apply moist and fatty substances; and he applies poultices, and uses warm and softening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the fetus is on his side, and you can make it even, then administer what we have said about a live child; but if one does not have the strength to do that, then pull it out in pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if it is administered to those who have said that abscesses come in the sea; and if bloodletting occurs, let it be stopped with astringents, and other remedies are administered.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly a child had died, then another was sewn over it, and the other died too.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time she got an abscess in her armpit, which swelled so much that it opened and began to ooze profusely.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the wound, and I thought for a long time, but could not heal it.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong attracting plaster, and one bone came out, and after a few days, some others.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I probed the wound, and put my hands inside it until the woman was in a better state; and she lived for a long time afterwards, although sometimes a little urine would leak out; and I have only mentioned this chapter because when a teacher discovers something strange, he should know how to provide relief.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	how to return the dislocated joint to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the press, with which one cuts into the books; and in .2 turns at .2 ears of .2 lines.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horn should be more subtle than the restrictor and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the tube should be half a finger wide, and the edges of the trees should be sharpened, and between the two edges there should be two stops of the same wood, which are fixed in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two stops are inserted into the mouth of the sea to open when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, with a more subtle and lighter appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the resemblance of tongs; and has at its two ends two adjustments, as you see, of a palm in length, and two digits in width; and when you see to open the wound to all the instrument, then let the woman lie on the bed, her feet hanging and her legs spread, then fit the two adjustments together in the wound, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs; then work your hand throughout the instrument, as you have done with tongs similarly, according to the quantity that you see to open the mouth of the wound, until the midwife does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all decorated, and their appearances are multiplied; and when the patient sees them prepared, his fear is increased, and he is more reluctant to undergo the procedure because of their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair about the instrument until you have prepared it, for their necessity is unavoidable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained in childbirth, you should instruct the patient to hold in her breath, and then make her sneeze with an emetic, and pinch her hands and nose; and if she passes gas through these means, that is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, he takes the pot and makes an opening in the lid, and puts herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as calendula, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water over fire; then put a stick into the opening in the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the wound, and hold it so that the vapors enter the wound; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then let the secondine dry quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this treatment and does not urinate, command the midwife to moisten her left hand with oil of sesamum or with a poultice of elderberries, and then insert it into her naturally, and find the second membrane; and when she has found it, grasp it and extend it little by little straight, so that the wound is not stretched during extraction; but she must move it slightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If the mouth of the wound is constricted, we have described the treatment of sneezing and fumigation with herbs; if it does not open with all that we have said, then beware of bleeding; but what is at the mouth of the wound, you should tie it to the thigh of the woman, then cleanse it with a four-drug ointment; then she will pass wind and recover, but still, when she passes wind, an evil odor comes to the stomach and head, and the patient suffers.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So then one should use appropriate fume: some of the ancients have tried smoke from watercress and dry figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used to smoke out the woman for the retention of flowers and afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It is made of glass like a cane, and the narrow end is placed in the wound, and the wide end above the coals; and the fumigation is over the charcoal, and the wound until it is healed, and then another one is started.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born without a perforated anus; instead, they have a small, narrow opening: therefore, the midwife should pierce this with her finger, and not with a sharp instrument, and keep the bandage from touching it; then she should put on warm milk mixed with wine and oil, and then treat the wound with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that he will be cured, then put a plug of wool in the wound, and leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes a sudden stop to the bleeding occurs in a wound or an abscess; then it must be stopped suddenly: then it should be dressed as we have said with a plug of wool.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the anus are nodules, and they grow larger than those that come from inside the anus, or in the space between its two parts, whether there is one fistula or multiple. And when this nodule becomes old, it opens up, and usually white pus or thin fluid emerges, and sometimes these fistulas become infected. They are recognized by the fact that the patient either expels them through defecation or they come out as wind, and sometimes they may burst out on their own.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that pierce all the way to the bladder, and halfway down the shaft of the penis; and they reach up to the hip joint, and to the scrotum.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes a persistent fistula in the anus that does not drain: and it is necessary to press your index finger into the anus, and insert a thin needle made of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is twisting, one must insert a thin tent made of lead or horse hair into the fistula as far as you can feel it with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no pus or wind emerges as we have said, then know that it has not broken through; so be quick about treating it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has reached the bladder or the urethra, then the urine flows out, and medicine cannot stop it.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced to the joint of the thigh, then the vein flows to the site; if there is twisting and the pain extends around, then it will settle down there, and ointments are of no use, neither suddenly nor over time; and in these persisting fistulas, there is no cure beyond hard work, and foolishness is the reward of those who meddle.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In one that is not persisting and not old, there is hope of recovery by iron, as I have experienced, and the patient lies on his back; and you raise his legs up to his thighs, and he bends his thighs towards his belly; then you pierce a tent made of bronze or lead, if there is twisting, as far as you can tell where the vein flows.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around his anus, then you must pierce with your index finger if the vein has not yet been pierced; and if it is uncovered where you feel between your finger and the flesh, then you know that it is persisting; so do not work on one who cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can still heal them, although it is rare; and the aid that one provides is to scorch with a fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; and pour everything hot into the fistula, as far as the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that those diseased tissues have been burned away, which are like a feather; and then cure with moist bandages with tallow, until those tissues come out; and then cure with ointment, closing up the wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it cannot be healed otherwise; and if pus enters between, and does not pierce all the way to the rectum which is at the fundament, and there is a thick covering of diseased tissue between your finger and the bandage, and you see the fistula continues below this covering towards the anus; then cut away the beginning of the fistula, and pour in hot water before the bandage, and then cauterize afterwards, as far as the top of the bandage; and the bandage will be delivered, and fall out; then scrape away those diseased tissues that look like a feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pus runs out, and goes between you and the wound, then cauterize it with fire or with medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Because fire cautery brings together two things: the burning of the joined flesh and the stanching of blood and the drying of moisture; then the treatment of tents with butter or ground substance until the bowels gush forth and the burnt flesh issues from the bowels; then treat the wound with sudatory poultices made of hard charcoal, and these are dry remedies.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes from the depth of the foundation, and is separated from the body, put your finger into it, and explore it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you sense the tent, and within it are threads or flesh, or it is close to piercing, then there is no other way but to seek salvation and hope through one of three methods: either cauterize as we have said, or cut to the bottom, or if you can, insert tents and treat as before; and do not go too deep, lest you cut into the lining that holds the foundation, and let the evacuations issue forth through the orifices as they may; then treat as we have said; perhaps it will be healed. Or remove that covering and cleanse after it has been cut from the foundation, either by tent or other pointed instrument; then medicate that infected flesh in the wound, as you can; then strive to heal the wound and prevent the fistula from spreading beyond the foundation: thus the patient will suffer less.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes they are fistulas according to this way: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side next to the foundation underneath the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the top according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he inserts a twisted thread into it, and inserts the tent along the entire thread into the fistula as far as the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is piercing in the margin of the foundation inside, then pull out the thread from that hole, so that you put your finger on the foundation; and pull the head of the thread, and bring the two heads together, and tighten them against each other, and leave it for one or two days; and sometimes they are tightened, until the threads scrape those cells that are between two, and dry up; then cure the wound until it is souded and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not drain, then have it drained in every way you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to cover with a bandage immediately after lancing, and then treat the wound, as we have said, until it has healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spathumile spiny, from which one makes the fistula, is very sharp on one side and smooth on the other; and not sharp where it should not be, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two types: they can be inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and some discharge blood, and there may be one or several of them, and they protrude from the anus and from the top of the anus; but those that protrude have little moisture, and sometimes a little yellow water or blood, and they take on the color of the body. The treatment for those who have them inside is to make the patient strain to move his bowels until the hemorrhoids appear, and then you can see the veins; then you must hurry and grasp them with tweezers, or hold them with your fingernail, then cut them at their roots; and if the nails cannot hold them because of moisture, they are grasped with a piece of cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois; then they are pulled out with the fingers, then cut, and powder some hot powdered cautery on top of them; or you can cauterize them as described in the chapter on cautery, then treat other hemorrhoids until he is cured; and if the anus cannot be cleared, cleanse the patient with a sharp and harsh enema to wash away what is inside the anus so that it can come out easily; when the patient strains and the veins are pushed out of the anus, the treatment is simple; then you grasp them with your fingernail or tweezers, cut them, and then treat them as we have said until he is cured and fears incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should perform the stitching in this manner: take a twisted thread and put it through a needle; then pull the thread from above and push the needle through from the other side, bringing the two ends of the thread together beneath the needle, leaving some slack; tighten the thread firmly, tie off the thread, remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, leaving one to stop any bleeding; then place a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate over the wound, and command the patient to rest; leave it until the stitches fall out, and then treat the wound with ointment and other remedies until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from dryness of the anus or rectum
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is dryness of the bowels within the intestines, caused by natural constriction, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should cut away at the tip of a wart or thorn with a spatula or your fingernail, removing the outer layer so that it does not become moist; then treat it until it scabs over as it should; and if it cannot scab over, repeat the scraping more aggressively than before, until it heals well and is fully removed; then treat it until it is completely healed.
dou fremit	when it trembles
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small appearance formed under the body, and they go very deeply; and sometimes the ant stings them, and they feel it as if dead from trembling, and it comes all over the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a needle from an goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place this needle on the trembling, until the purple circle around the trembling; then turn your hand all around the needle so that you grab all around the trembling, and drive it deeply, and pull out the trembling by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit to make a candle of bronze or iron according to this shape, let it be thin beneath and drawn out on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce it, so that the candle can be held in the hand and pressed against the shin. And if you see fit, cauterize the shins as described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes an enema is made of silver or brass, or of melted or hammered copper; and sometimes they are made of small and large instruments, depending on those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are administered for the treatment of children, and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large enema is above wide, or the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And it has a decrease where the bellies are tied, as you see, and the intestines are pierced inside; and it has two openings on one side, and one on the other; and the belly is where one puts the medicine of a beast's bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small openings, and there is an inch of space between each opening, then tie into these openings a strong thread of twisted thread in the shape of X or around, and assemble the belly so that it is like a goat; and when the medicine is inside, then tie it to the instrument in front with a strong string, then cleanse; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or egg white or a similar substance, then plug it up lightly; then the minister should squeeze his fingers together until he is all wet, then remove the plug, and let the patient lie with his legs exposed to the air, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him hold it as long as he can; and if he sleeps for a night afterward, it will be even better.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you treat him with a syringe for dysentery, and the medicine rushes out quickly, then repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the anus or an abscess, let the catheter be as thin as for a child; and the shape of the thin catheter that presses on the skin is:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will discuss manual and medicinal treatments according to their properties.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and according to what makes them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by a blow of stone or sword and knife, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar objects; or they are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or head, or foot, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, one should take care if it is due to a blow from a stone or similar object, and the skin is still intact and the wound is large, and you quickly doubt a hot abscess: then have him bleed with the cephalic vein itself if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the bleeding be in the opposite direction of the injured part; and let the patient avoid fullness from wine and rich foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, then let him lessen his food intake and neither drink wine nor eat meat; and put cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in astringent wine, on the wound if hot abscesses come from it; and if there is no hot abscess, then put powder on the wound when it has all its blood and has not been moved by the air, which I will speak about a little later; and if the burn has been moved by the air, then put some ointments on it until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, such as from a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together with stitches, then bring them together with sutures, as I will describe for wounds of the abdomen, of the chest.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and it can be reached with a finger, but only just, then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as testicles and cooked wheat, as well as meat, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a boil on the skin, and it is not near the bone, then lance it and let out the pus; then treat it with medicine. And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which pulsates, and it cannot be staunched by medicine, then tie it off with a thread; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is easy; you should apply this powder which causes sores to heal as soon as the fire has burned them.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it tightly, until it is firmly attached to all its blood; and then tie it well, and leave it without loosening, if it does not swell; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one makes it only with chalk, when one doesn't have incense or dragon's blood, but so long as the wound is moved by fire.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has been moved by fire, it should be left as it is without applying any of this powder; instead, put on some digestive ointments or a poultice made from barley flour mixed with water and honey until it becomes soft; then treat it with other treatments until it heals.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if there is a fracture with the wound, and it is small, then I will extract it with subtle tweezers; and I will tell you later about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	wounds to the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, there should be no other treatment than leaving the wound uncovered and not applying anything constricting, because it harms the nerves and makes them retract; and nothing cold should be applied to the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but the medicine should be warm, like hot water washed in warm water, and mixed with rose oil, and cooked washed also in warm water, and other stones of this kind, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then cut and ligate the vessels, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is deep and it is bleeding and full of pus, then pierce it or a lower spot; and if the artery is cut and bleeding ensues, then ligature it, and cauterize if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the passage for food is blocked, then cut along the windpipe on the throat's collarbone, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape; and then ligature it properly, and leave it for a few days, then cleanse with cleansing ointments until it heals; and if the wound has left an impression in the bone, then pierce it; and if there are bone fragments, then draw them all out if you can, and those that you cannot reach, leave them be until the wound heals, and clean the wound and ligature the exit; and if the wound is fresh, then apply powder over the powder as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have described in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a strike from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then examine whether the wound breathes winds from the injury: thus you know that the wound is deadly; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put the powder to it in the first hour, nor bind it for the blood that seeps out, pierces through, returns to the body, and heals the patient; but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, then place old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture, and let the patient sleep on the wound for three, four, or more days; then no spasms, tremors of the body, or pains in the limbs will come; and when you see good signs, then you know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it therefore with poultices and other remedies until it is healed; and if it will not heal, and the wound remains open, then know that there is a fistula; treat it as it should be treated.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, in the face or back, then treat it as we have said before; if it is large, close it with stitches; and if it is small, treat it with powder; and if it has pierced deep into the bone, and pieces of it are visible, then clean the wound and pull out any foreign bodies; and if they are not visible, let the wound fester to draw out any foreign objects; and for other wounds in other parts of the body, judge as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from rupturing of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	There are great, medium and small ruptures of the belly; from the large wound sometimes the intestines or nerves of the intestines protrude, causing pain when they are touched; and stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because one must stitch up the intestines little by little, warming them gradually as they are stitched; for the intestines swell as soon as they feel cold, so they must be stitched up little by little, and it is better to treat a smaller wound in this way, as one can stitch up the intestine gradually back into place rather than all at once. And know that there are four types of ruptures of the belly: the two common types occur with stitching of the belly, and with stitching of other wounds on the body; and the two other types are specific to the belly, and I will describe each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and something from the intestines has come out, and it is difficult to put back in, it is by one of two ways: either because of the size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to coldness.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: moisten a sponge or soft cloth in lukewarm water only, or cook in squint water and cypress and spikenard, and warm the intestines until the swelling is removed; and sometimes this wine constrictor helps, and it is better to use it solely for deflation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling go down, then moisten the intestines with water or altee and mallows that have been cooked, for through this the entrance is restricted by a little; and if it cannot enter, then make a small cut in the wound with an instrument that is used to scrape out hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is better than cutting, which one should not do without great necessity; and the instrument for splitting is: insert it into the curve and push out, and see the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, then put them back according to their natural shape in their proper place, if you can, because this is worth it.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is low in the abdomen, you should make the patient lie on his back and elevate his legs above his head; and if it's high in the abdomen, he should be positioned so that his head and feet are higher than his torso, and if the rupture is on one side of the abdomen, then the affected part should be elevated higher than the other. This advice holds true for both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what is readily available to you; then, hold in your hand an instrument that covers the entire wound, and bring the edges together; this is the common method of suturing. Take a needle or several needles according to the size of the wound, leaving two fingers' width from the top of the wound, and thread a strong needle with one or two strands through both edges of the skin and the subcutaneous tissue beneath; then, tie off the thread around the needle so that it pulls the edges together. Repeat this process as needed according to how many needles you require, until the entire wound is closed. The needles should be medium-sized, not too thin or too thick; thin needles can pierce through the flesh and skin, while thick ones may not be able to enter at all. Tie off the threads around the needles so that they don't cut into the patient's skin when they sleep, and place tents or pieces of cloth over the needle heads to keep them in place. Leave the sutures until the wound has healed. This method of suturing with needles is most suitable for small wounds. I once sewed up a man who had been stabbed in the abdomen; the wound was more than a palm wide, and his intestines protruded out by two palms; I closed the wound while it was still inside the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him back the intestine, which had been outside for 24 hours; I sewed up the wound and it healed in 15 days.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they had judged him to be dead, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where there was no medicine or ointment available; and I placed old cotton over the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you about two proper methods of suturing: take the needle and insert it from the outside into the inside of the body; when it has pierced through to the other side, hold the needle in place with your thumb or finger on the spot where you inserted the needle, and then bring the needle out through another spot on the inside and draw it back out to the outside. The principle behind this type of suturing is that you sew just like a leatherworker sews leather, going back and forth between the two sides of the wound until the suturing is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.
