The second method of suturing, which Galen describes correctly, is as follows: bring the two parts together naturally and apply one end of a silk thread to the other, in such a way that you pierce one side only, and leave the two ends of the wound; then return the needle and pierce through from the outside part into the inside, through both ends of the wound; then pierce through both ends from the outside part into the inside, through two other ends of the silk thread on the opposite side; this is the best and most common method of suturing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this, and some testify to it: one should sew the abdomen with two needles, each with a thread through it; then one should push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew up wounds; and know that when the wound is in the middle of the abdomen, the suturing is more difficult than in other places in the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are as for other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound full of blood, so that the fire has moved it, then put back the intestines, and close the wound; then put on the powder of the healing charcoal, and if the fire has moved it, then apply some ointment that is present, until the wound heals; then tie the threads, and sew the sutures, and the mirach; then treat the wound as for the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicine, then put on old cotton, as soon as it begins to heal, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need any other medicine in various dispositions where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will affect the principal members, then moisten a light woolen cloth in tempered warm oil, or in rose oil, and place it around the angers, and under the armpits; and if there is pain or swelling in the bowels, and it happens many times, then enema with tepid black wine, and especially if the swelling comes to the intestines; and pierce it from within, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "young" cannot heal when they are damaged, and this is due to the thinness of their walls, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of their nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the thread jumps out of the wound, put it back as it was while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, you should tie up the area which is black so that no more bleeding occurs, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut away what is between the stitch, and let the two ends hang loose below the wound until it is time to extract them when the wound has healed.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rot of boiling water
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are severed and the wound is small, one can sometimes heal it in this way: I saw a man who was pierced by a lance in his abdomen; the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became a fistula, from which he passed stools and gases; I treated him according to my ability and continued to suturing until it healed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewing up, I doubted that the patient had harm in his belly; and he had no harm, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in such a way: take a needle with a large eye, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the needle has passed through, put it over both lips so that it presses his mouth closed; and then tie off the thread, and it will remain so that he cannot untie it, then put another needle after in the same way as before, until the wound is completely sewn up; and then cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If these wounds are in the intestine and no harm comes to the patient, and one can sew up the intestine with a slender thread cut from an animal's intestine, in such a way: take the end of this intestinal thread which is well charred, and then tie to the end of this thread a slender linen thread wound around it, then put the thread through the needle, and sew up the intestine and tie off the thread; and this manner of sewing with a needle is not certain except according to hope and expectation; and if the wound is large and broad, especially when it is in one of the intestines, there is no healing unless with great skill.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula, wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it wakes up, is universally called a "fistula", and especially when it is swollen and becomes bow-shaped.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the verdant nodule, made hard and white, where there is no pain, and is just as bowed as the feather of a bird; and sometimes it is clear and bowed, and sometimes thick; sometimes small, and sometimes large enough; and I have already spoken about these causes in the division of wounds: that any wound which is not healed, and there is no pus, is due to one of nine causes: namely, because of the smallness of blood or body; or because of its wickedness; or because there is hard matter within it, and on the lips, which does not allow pus to form; or there is too much inflammation; or the site is poor, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good for treatment; or because the corruption is of a pestilential nature; or because the region's property is late in digestion, slow in healing, and swollen by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I should let you know about the treatment of fistula which is done by handiwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and from arteries, and from nerves, or from the sinus, or from the intestines, or from the bladder, or from any of the ribs, or from the spine of the back, or from any joint of the hands or feet; and also where they occur in the principal part of a limb, and in similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this way are of grief sanation, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it being understood, then take a tent of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, so that it may be quiered; and if the fistula is crooked, then search it with a fine tent of lead, for the lead bends around the tortuositeit; and if the fistula has many openings, and you cannot properly search it by tents, then cleanse it through one of the openings with a clyster, for moisture goes from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then quier it bloody to your ability so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and is chewed em by depth, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where they feel it most; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places I have mentioned to you, then treat it according to what I have told you, and remove the putrefied matter and rotten flesh that are within; and then cure it until it is healed; and if the fistula is very deep from a straight place, then you must cope it deeply as much as you can, then put moist tents in medicine ague, and fill them up to the head of the fistula so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; and then put ointments on it until it is healed, and if it is not healed by this method, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cope it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve in the limbs causes you grief, as we have said, and if the bone is exposed and there is decay and darkness, then treat it with cautery until the decay is completely removed, then cure the wound with healing ointments until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and becomes swollen again as before, know that you have not gone deep enough: then open and probe until you reach the bottom, and remove all the decay, then restore the bone; and if it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the decay is too deep for you to reach; then let nature take its course, and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with tweezers, or with an instrument suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, one by one; and if moisture causes a contrary effect, without error or fear, then dry and cauterize, and apply ointments to heal the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, then place something on the wound to encourage pus formation, and let it remain until the pus has formed around the bone, and then the bones will come out more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as the leg or thigh, then cut away only 肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉腐肉
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of about thirty who had a pain in his leg from an internal cause, so that the matter came to the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it; but they looked at it because of their folly and worked on it until the abscess opened and a lot of matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many holes appeared in it through which the fluid from the body flowed; and many doctors treated him for two years, and there was no one with wisdom in the art of medicine, so I was called to see him, and I saw his leg and the remedies they used to treat him, and what was flowing out of the holes into a large container; and the skin of the young man turned red and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I placed a tent over one of the holes and then examined all the openings, finding that they connected with each other throughout the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened, therefore, and probed one of the openings until I exposed a portion of the bone, which I found to be corrupted and perforated, and the corruption extended to the bone within; I probed what appeared to me to be the corruption, and believed that there was no other corruption except that which I removed; and then I began to heal the wound with strong medicines for a long time, but it would not heal; and then I probed again, and exposed the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, which I probed and then removed, and labored to heal the spot; but I could not, though I probed around a palm's breadth of the bone, and cut away all its soft parts, then healed it with medicines; and it was cured and healed rapidly, and there was no need to probe the wound again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often because of the bloodletting he bled a lot, but he was completely healed and in the place of the bone a hard lump formed, and he had a good disposition and did not suffer any harm or ill effects in every way, neither when walking nor when standing.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, one should treat it in this way: take a thread and tie it to the top of the exposed bone, and instruct someone to pull it upwards; and take another larger piece of linen and tie it over the lump on the bone, and tie it at the top so that you draw the rotten flesh underneath towards the bottom, and uncover the flesh above where you see the need for treatment, so that the thread does not cut into the flesh; and place a hot iron or a wooden block underneath the bone to press down on the rotten flesh; and one should keep doing this as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and do it again later.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is broken and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover all the flesh; then place a firebrand underneath, and then cut away the corruption from one part to another, and cut away the healthy tissue around the site of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut into the corrupted joint and cut the bone where it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no need to cut except at the joint; and if the corruption is at the wrist of the hand, or at the wrist of the foot, then this thing is very strong, but nevertheless you must inquire into this corruption, how it appears to you; and cleanse it in every way that you can, but be careful not to damage the vein or nerve; and know that there are many types of cutting instruments for treating broken bones, depending on the structure of the bone, its appearance, thickness, thinness, length, and hardness; therefore, one must prepare a tool for each type of treatment. You will learn which tool you need according to your knowledge of this art and the characteristics of the disease; then choose the tool that is most appropriate.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head may be injured either internally or externally; and when you have treated this injury with medicine, and it does not help, then cover the affected limb up to the point where the injury is, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater evil, from the defect in the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, as if burned by fire, and after the blackness there is swelling; then this corruption spreads from limb to limb, and throughout the body; therefore be quick about covering it, and if it is due to the sting of some venomous creature, such as a sea-scorpion, adder, or similar, and the injury is on the head, then cover it, and do not give it any space to spread to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, then cover at the joint so that the injury does not spread to the arm; and if it is on the arm, then cover at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, then it is fatal, and there is no treatment beyond the degree of its virtue; and thus do for any injury to the foot: if it is in the first joint, then cover after the other joint; and if it is on the foot, then cover the whole foot; and if it ascends into the leg, then cover at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, then there is no remedy but to cut off the limb, and the manner of covering it is to tie it above and below, and extend one implement down from one binding, and another implement up from the other binding, and cut away the flesh between the two bindings to a width of one span, so that the bone is exposed; then cover it with a silk cloth, and place a linen cloth on each side so that the silk does not touch the healthy part, and cause further injury or abscesses.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the wound gently, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete, then bind the injured member with a suitable ligature and cure it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his sleep: he developed a darkness that looked like a burn, and this corrosion first appeared on his big toe of the foot, spreading to cover the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he covered his foot and healed; and a long time after, the corrosion returned to his finger, and he came to me, and I applied reflective remedies after purification of the body, but could not stop the corrosions; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, for I had hope of repelling the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the man's strength was weak; and he despaired completely, returned home, covered his hand, and healed; and I have never heard of anyone else doing this except for those who need it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Occasionally an abscess develops in a fleshy area, and remains for so long that it causes a great gathering of pus; and then it bursts and pierces, and the pus flows out, leaving the wound open like a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as a piece of cloth, and does not heal over to the bone or nerve, and such a disease is called 'sore', but is not called a 'fistula'; but if it is so extended that it reaches the bone deeply, then it is called a 'fistula'; and the skin is such that you can wrap around this skin all around, and especially when it is thin, like a piece of cloth; and it does not heal over from its decay.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have reason to believe that the skin is healing over and the decay is not deep, and the flesh of the skin is thick, then cleanse with a clyster as follows: examine whether the breast is swollen, and the pus within has a foul odor, then prepare an Egyptian medicine thus: take ash, and oil, and litharge, in equal parts, and put the medicine into a vessel over a fire until it turns red, and becomes as thick as honey; and then take some according to your need, and dissolve it in water and honey, and clyster the breast, and squeeze out the pus; leave the medicine inside for two hours, then squeeze it out again; do this repeatedly, until the breast is cleaned out and the pus removed; and sometimes a clyster of ash-water is used when the Egyptian medicine is not available, and you take vine-ash, and pour water over it, then strain off the liquid, and clyster with this until you know that the breast is cleansed; if the patient cannot bear either the Egyptian medicine or the ash-water, then clyster with water and honey to which a little litharge has been added; or you can clyster with honey and wine in which the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the wound bleed; and when you have done this, and you have reason to believe that the breast is cleansed, then clyster with something that causes flesh to grow in it, and you take diaphoretic ointment, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or you can clyster with other medicines and ointments of which I have spoken in the section on ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the tube of the clyster cannot enter, then widen it a little with a sharp instrument, and put in some of the Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is widened enough; and if the wound is very large, then cut away only as much as will allow the clyster to enter, and if the opening that drains the pus is above, then cover it below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Because when the bowels are in perfect health, one does not leave excrement in them; and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, then prepare in such a way that the bowels move to the lowest place they can reach, for when the bowels are healthy, one does not leave excrement in them, and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, then prepare in such a way: let the bowels move slightly downward, and do not leave anything of the bowels; and take consolative medicines to place over the wound, and they must be placed on top of a linen drape that covers all of the wound; then cover the wound firmly at its strongest point, making the opening larger than it was before, and apply a soothing ointment on the other drape according to the size of the wound, and place it on the wound to alleviate the bowels, and do not remove the large drape for several days; and that which is placed over the wound, often remove to eliminate the bowels, and examine what comes from them, whether it is venom or pus or blood, or digested or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature that rises on top of the wound, then know that the breast has healed, and approach the wound; and then untie it in the morning, or at noon, and when you untie the wound, change the other drape, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast milk flows low and indigestible after many days, know that the breast does not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons creep slowly, you must not despair of health, for health draws near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are wounds whose wound-fluid seeps slowly into the flesh, and others that do the opposite; and if indigestible bile erupts from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healing; and if the breast is slow to heal and distant, apply dry medicines moist in substance but dry in virtue, as with diaphanous ointment, for it contains a great deal of vitriol, and that is the last medicine; take diaphanous ointment, which is made with rose oil, and arrosa of old wine equal in substance; then cook it down and use it as needed; and if diaphanous ointments are not available, take myrrh, aloe, and incense, grind them to powder over honey when it is on the fire; then glue a cloth with it and apply it to the breast, and at times administer aristology for a long time, and roots of celestial lilies, which is like flour of vesicants and centaury; and use simples or compounds: grind them to powder and put over the honey I mentioned above, and use as needed; and if the cure is slow, and not healed by this cure, then know that corruption is deep-seated, and makes impressions in bones, or in limbs, or in viscera; so treat the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaris is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or occasionally in other places; and when it becomes infected, and no action is taken, an abscess forms, and it runs and discharges pus as far as the root of the nail, and sometimes all the way to the bone; and erosion occurs right down to the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the area around the digit becomes swollen, and the colour is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the previous section, and the treatment is ineffective, then you must cut away all the excess tissue that remains beneath the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cautery is a great help if the bone and nail are both healthy; and if the nail is pushing down on the flesh, and beginning to grow into it, causing inflammation, then you must put a thread under the nail so that it pushes the flesh upwards, and then carefully cut away the flesh, using burning and corrosive medicines to remove all of it; then treat the wound with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and pull it out, because as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see the corruption spreading, then cut it in half at the joint as previously described, then treat the wound until it heals; and if it becomes infected and swollen, and causes great pain, then you must treat it first; then cut the nail of the affected finger diagonally from above, and be careful that the cut does not go all the way to the flesh under the nail, because the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, place something on it to soothe the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two toenails that sometimes grow on people's hands by chance are sometimes all flesh, and sometimes they have bones, and sometimes they have nails, and some grow from the root of the joint, or from one of the toes.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born with an extra tooth in his gum will not move, but he who is born at the joint of the gum may move; the one whose gum is fleshy has a light wound, thus: cut it at its root with a wide spathe.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; if you hold it tightly.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one who is born with an extra tooth in the gum at the back, you should first cut away the round flesh to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable silk thread, then heal it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together come by birth, or by joint wound, or by burn from fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Then you should cut that seam so that the gums fit together according to their natural shape; then put between two tents or dampened cloth in rose oil so that they do not stick together; or put between two pieces of thin lead, until the gum is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If sealing occurs on one of his hands with the palm, then treat that wound as it should be treated.
des vils	of the villainous
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are thick enveloped vessels filled with melancholy superfluities, which come in many parts of the body; and they occur more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than in others.Et plus que en celles de celz qui montent a cheval et sont plus en trais et demourent en lieu.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him a cleansing enema, and then the basilicon ointment.Et li amonestre et la maniere dou saine et dou cautere, et que il doit faire, si te veult dire.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure with fire is in two ways: one is that one cauterizes and draws out the black blood; and the other way is that you open a vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done in this way: first, raise the leg with very hot water until the large veins are made small, then stretch the leg from above the thigh to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two or three, with a broad incision, and then open and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the virtue of the medicine can endure; and then tie it off, and instruct him to apply a poultice of black cole on top; and restart the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are closed up, and bandage the wound.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment for this is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there are many hairs, then put it in the bath, and pour hot water over the leg until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then press the vein from the top down to the knee, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin at the base of the nail, and scrape the vein on each side, until it appears when you feel it; and you will see it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it looks like a white cord; then tie the thread under, so that it is lifted from the skin, and then it can be pulled at another hook, as before; then make another incision, or several if necessary, then lift and cut into the leg to the toe, then pull and lift until you reach the second incision; then pull it out of the incision, until it is all out, and then cut it off; and if you cannot pull and lift it, tie a strong double thread under it, and tie and pull it, and tie it under the thread, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out; be careful not to cut it, because if it cuts, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and it causes harm to the patient. And when you have finished treating it, put moistened wool in wine and rose oil over the wound site; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it twistedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cauterizes the vein is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not pierce the vein; and it is of a gross curve, for if it were subtle, it would pierce the vein, but it must be thick as we have said, and thus is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot regions where no herbs or trees grow, and in land without moisture; and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the pustules that come under the skin, as do snakes and worms, growing between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that a great inflammation comes in the leg, then the place changes, and the wound begins to come out forcefully, just as the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the shoulder opens, you should wrap a piece of plank about three and a half to four inches around it, and the knot, and let the plank hang on the leg, and every time it comes out of its socket, wrap it around the plank and the knot; and if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the rest, but do not cover the root while it is still coming out; for if you cover it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and swelling in the spot, and for this reason it should be treated little by little until the head, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this wound is as long as five or ten palm-lengths, and a man came to me once who had one that issued ten palm-lengths, and when you cover it, plug the hole or opening, and bore to the bottom so that all of it comes out, and evacuate the matter within, and apply healing medicines to the spot for several days, then treat it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein bleeds profusely, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or the leg, and much blood flows out, and from which it rains; therefore treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	from worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "cow disease" in our land because it often affects cows. It is caused by a small worm that grows between the skin and flesh, moving throughout the body, ascending and descending, until it breaks out of the skin, often causing much damage. It is similar to the harm done by worms, snakes, and earthworms in the belly; and one fears its malice, for when it moves through the body and reaches the head, it can enter and destroy the eye. This has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and treated, you cannot hold it back except when it bleeds: therefore, you must tie the area above and below with a strong string tied tightly, then press on it from above and draw it out forcefully; and if the pus is deep in the flesh, and you do not bring it out, cauterize it with fire until it comes out; and the greatest harm that it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the eye, tighten under it firmly, then press on it from above and draw it out forcefully; and one must use the cleansing of the body with medicines that dissolve bad humors, and use cauterization with flesh-corroding substances for pus.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from wind
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vacering" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some members, and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I uncovered her arm, and saw a small swelling on the vein of the arm; and a little later, I saw it rise up like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything else, as bright as silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain left that spot, and settled in the shoulder, and then a little later ran through the whole body, until it reached the other arm; then she told me that she was spinning around the body, just as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how she moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease progress in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I have often seen pain move from one place to another, but not as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because women's bodies are dry, and their veins exposed, and this windiness appears constrained for this reason, and not according to this reason in those who are plump, and have moist bodies and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels the pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then press above and below gently, and then apply a poultice until that forced wind leaves its place; and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it yourself, then treat it with those who expel winds, such as foul pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the part of the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of them is that there are some with large points, and small, and barbed, and smooth; and some with two angles, and some with tongues, and some with pieces; and those that break in a limb break in two ways: either in a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, stomach, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she falls in any of these places on the body, and you see the signs of death that I will tell you about later, then you must be wary of removing this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many cases; and if you do not see these bad signs, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of trepanation when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and if there is a blow to the brain above the cerebrum, are scalp-lacerations and cuts and blisters and redness, inflammation and reddening of the tongue, spasms and loss of consciousness, vomiting of blood; and perhaps there is bleeding from the nose or ears; and often they lose their speech and voice; and if there is white moisture oozing from the wound like pus, and also a bruise-like appearance, then be wary of trepanation, and pull out the arrow if it is not deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the seventh are that it lies near the left breast, and feels as though it were stuck to something hard, and not hollow; and sometimes the seventh is mute like the pulses, and discharges black blood, and there comes a chill and cold sweat, and syncope: then know beyond doubt that death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow wound that affects the lung is spitting foam from the wound, and a swollen throat, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces the covering of the foot, it affects the small bones; and there is great pain and swelling and discomfort, and the patient feels pain throughout their shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach, by chance some undigested food may come out through the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow pierces the intestines in the abdomen, and no feces escape through the rear end, then there is no hope for a cure or for removing the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the arrow pierces the bladder, and urine escapes and flows outward, and the patient feels intense pain, know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, armpit, spine of the back, hip, thigh, and leg, and similar limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	Once an arrow struck a man in the jaw near the root of the ear; I probed it and pulled it out from under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without any numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I extracted an arrow from the jaw of a boy which had pierced through the fatty tissue under the eye socket, and the arrow was lodged there, with only its tip protruding towards the nose; the arrow was as thick as a Turkish bowstring, and made of iron, and light in weight; the boy was healed and no ill effects followed.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arab arrow that had pierced his ears; I cut off the barbs, and pulled gently until I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I extracted an arrow from a man's body that had pierced his chest or belly, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days, his condition did not worsen; so I cut into the shaft of the arrow, and removed the barbed tip, pulling it out without any adverse effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man with an arrow in his back, and the wound is sewn up on top; as long as the arrow remains inside him, and his natural functions are not impaired, nor any harm found in any of his natural processes.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you will see another man whom an arrow has pierced in the face, and the wound is sewn up; he remains thus without great pain, and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And took an arrow to the home of the prince king, who was shot in the eye, and it was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was all drawn out I was called to the cure after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I wanted to probe it with a subtle instrument, and I didn't feel anything; and he felt stabbing and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I applied a digestive and atraumatic poultice to the site, so that the swelling would go down; and the mark of the arrow appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice again and again, and the wound healed quickly, and the patient suffered for a long time, as long as he felt the arrow in his eye; and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed medicine made of corrosive earth on the wound for several days until it was exposed and I could feel the tip of the arrowhead; then I applied the medicine to the wound opening so that the head of the arrow appeared clearly, and after about four months the wound healed completely and I was able to extract the arrow with tweezers. I probed and manipulated the wound with instruments for several days until one day I was able to grasp it with well-made tweezers, as described at the end of this chapter, and extracted it, healing the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they believed that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; so I restored it and the wound was closed and the patient fully healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Here I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care into what I do not say, because books cannot encompass everything; but wise masters consider well about very few things, and about what is present and lacking to them, they find new work, and new instruments, in the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows grow in the members where they are stuck in two ways: either by the place where they enter or by another part; and that which grows out by the place where it enters is an arrow entering into muscular tissues, and sometimes it grows out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not grow out now, then leave it as long as the tissue around it becomes rotten and the outlet is relieved; and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, then leave it for several days, and move it every day; and then it will grow out, and if it does not, then pierce through to the very tip of a subtle forest, as long as the outlets around are enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the skull and goes to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents which I have mentioned appear in the patient: then do not extract it, but let it be until it becomes even after a few days, for if the arrow goes to the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not go to the brain, and the patient remains for several days without any bad symptoms, then prepare an instrument for extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very swollen and cannot come out, then administer blisters around it, as I have told you; then clean the area until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged deep in the body where it cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the body; and if you feel it, extract it with an appropriate instrument; and if because of the depth of the wound and the penetration of the arrow there is no bone, nerve, or vein in the way, then open the wound widely; and if there are ears on the arrow by which it is lodged, remove the flesh around them from both sides as far as you can, and then bend or twist the ears of the arrow so that you can extract it; and be careful not to break the arrow, lest you push it further in.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot on one try, then leave it until the wound around it is swollen; then pull it out, for extraction is eased.
