Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes it contrary, then administer what we have said about the cure in its chapter; and guard against incising the nerve and the vein, and put in a splint how you can best pull out the arrow without peril, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the shape he was in when the arrow fell into him, for that is the greatest help there is. And if you cannot do it that way, then put him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes out from another place, or something is seen to come out of it, or the skin is swollen in an obvious way so that one can see or feel it: cut on top of it, until the tweezers can grab it, and then pull it out; thus jump out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is stuck in the bone, rotate your hand rapidly, forcing it into the bone and widening the opening; then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it and try again to pull it out until it comes out; and if there is a piece of the arrow inside, then take it out all at once; and if the shaft is broken, and you see that you can administer a bout, then administer the instrument chewed, so that the point of the arrow enters into the chew of the instrument; and then pull out, and if the arrow is chewed, then put the instrument with its point entering in to ease the extraction.Et s’il aduit que li saiette sont entres en l’estrument cheveit, et ne puisent issir, si failles de la tenaile sus la cheveure de l’estrument tant qu’i soient pres ens, et puis i triche; car il aduit que li saiettes, quant il sont entres en li estraments cheveitz, qu’il se tenaint le plus fort par la cheveure.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow has touched [the wound], then you must cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can; then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the arrow pierces the foot or leg or stomach or bladder or side, and it is deep, and you can cut it out; then be careful not to cut into the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then close the wound, if necessary; and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to an owl's beak; see the diagram.
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the broad-headed arrowhead is also like the feather of a bird, to catch on the tip of the arrow, just as its shape is:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of tongs for pushing and probing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common body veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins that heal: in the head there are XVI, namely: two batons located behind the ears, called the "herbech"; and the II arteries that are in the II temples, visible; and II veins that are in the II corners of the II eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the II windpipes that are in the neck; and the II veins that are above the lips, these are the veins called "augeherich"; and the II veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly used for bleeding are five in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, located on the left side of the neck, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "fast", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is located on the right side of the neck, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the cubital fossa, and it is that one through which bleeding is done, which opens clearly above the elbow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the little and ring fingers, and it has two branches; and in the leg there are three veins: one is below the crease of the elbow on the left side of the neck, and the second is at the ankle on the right side of the neck; and the vein that is called  "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of veins that are behind the ears is helped by old catarrhs and by emigration; and the qualities of the bleeding, as I told you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then wring the patient's neck with a rope until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places hanging from the head; then hold them in your fingers and where you feel the pulse under your fingers, sign there; then take the lance and pierce under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upstream, and pierce through the skin and the vein well with both hands, and let the blood out until you see it; then tie it off and stop it, until it is healed; and I have already said about incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the temples, is useful for long-standing migraine, and for sore eyes and habitual obtalmia, and for the body of tears and agues in the eyes; and the quality of the bleeder is as I have said: and it is that the patient strains his neck so that the two veins appear clearly; and feel the pulse under your thumb, and then sign with your finger; then raise the vein at the top of your finger and insert the lancette underneath, and raise the vein at the top, and cup it, as you have done in the other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their binding and their release at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein in the forehead is just as bad as the bleeding from the cephalic vein in old diseases of the face, and in hemiplegia and paralysis; and the qualities are such that the patient turns his neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point over the vein, and press firmly with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the amount that you see; then loosen the neck of the patient, and ligate the vein until it is healed, and sometimes the operation is done with a large flamethrower.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not appropriate for the flames to be too sharp; and heal across, because the bone is close by, and perhaps break the flames when they are fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the eyelids helps with styes, and paralysis, and redness, and inflammation of the eye, and diseases of the face; and the qualities of their bleeding are such that the patient turns his neck by twisting some ligament, as before; then he is bled, and the bleeding should be through the transverse vein, a little from the long vein, with a slightly larger flamethrower, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps they will break; then draw blood, as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein in the nose is good for ague, and for a violent fever, and for facial diseases, such as migrains and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient squeezes his neck, then pulls out his nose to your left hand, takes a long, thin flame, and inserts it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein doesn't open well otherwise, and the blood will start flowing immediately; and don't go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then ligate it for one night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of the two sinuses helps with strangulation of the throat, and with the beginning of measles, and many diseases, and with empyema, and with ulceration, and with herpes, and with ulcers; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient squeezes his neck from underneath on both sides, as we have said; and let the master stand over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then bleed the vein for a long time quite widely, then draw the blood temperately, or as much as is needed; then do the same in the other vein, then loosen the ligature, and squeeze both veins gently so that the patient does not choke; and let it be until morning so that the wound may heal.
de la sainie des leivres	of bleeding gums
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Here is the translation: The bleeding of the veins in the lips above helps with sores in the mouth, and gum corruption, and splits in the lips, and the pain of teeth and gums.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of bleeding are to have the patient sit before you and strain their neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by being black, and by having around them small black veins: so compress the one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you doubt, then compress the largest of each side, and likewise do with the two veins that are above and below, for it is a similar manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of veins that are beneath the tongue is helped after the bleeding of the cephalic vein; this is done by constricting the throat, and for diseases of the eye and mouth; and the quality of the bleeding should be such that the patient seizes between your hands in front of the sun, and releases the tongue, and looks underneath on each side for a black vein: therefore bleed both, and do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the head from which one usually bleeds are bled in two ways: either with a piercing flame of a large myrtle twig, or with a subtle olive wood stick as thin as a toothpick, and is called "anesil"; and they are large and thin according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the candle flame is very important, and it should be as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the flat veins of the head that contain thick and obvious blood; and this is the shape of the olive wood stick:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and suitable for bleeding the subtle veins where there is thin, yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that are under the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen; and the doctor must cauterize it bleeding, and protect the artery underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he pierces the artery and bleeding occurs, it must be stopped as I said before; but the flame should not be grasped, only trimmed like a candle.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic does not open obviously, then you must probe it and change to another vein; or take some blood from him, or cauterize the vein in his arm: it will open obviously; and cauterize it with the flame anesil, as we have said before.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to find the location of the cautery, then you must stretch out the arm and feel for the pulse; then mark the spot inside, and then tie up the arm, and cauterize the vein with the anesil flame; and be careful not to pierce the artery when you see the spot puffed up, because that is the artery: avoid it therefore.Et si tu ne puet aler plus a l’endercheure, si covient que tu retournes et saines la voinne dou flaime anesil; car li sang qui vout sortisse, si est de l’artere, ou de la veine.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it spurt upwards like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that this is blood from an artery: therefore hurry up, and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, as often happens; tie up the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move it until the patient is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not staunched and it flows, and you have no medicine, then compress the artery as it opens, for that is where the blood comes from; and stop the flow of blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of white willow bark, split it and take one half and tie it on firmly until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, then stop it with the powders that stanch blood, as we have said; but the stopping of the bleeding does not matter much in most cases because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The bleeding from an artery in the middle [of the body] is helped by it drawing blood from the head above and the body below because it is made of basil and cedar, as we have said; and the surgeon must be careful not to damage the nerve underneath, and if he cuts too deep into it, and inflames and injures it, and perhaps prevents healing; and this nerve often opens up, and if it does not open in some men because of its thinness, then you should treat it with the instrument anesil; and be careful of the nerve as much as you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, they cut it deeply.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein in the head, if it bleeds, aids the eyes; and one should bleed it with a flame from an olive or myrtle brand, for it is the safest of all veins, since it has neither nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, one should seek the lightest place, and not hurt at all if one misses the first time, and try again; and by chance, some men's parts may become swollen when they miss the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not done merely to maintain health and prevent illness; bleeding is performed in one of three veins: the head, the arm, or the leg. It should be done at the beginning of Lent, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of digestion are apparent. One should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bleeding which is administered for illnesses has no fixed time, but when there is a need, at any hour and at all times; and children should not be bled until they are 14 years old, nor women who are pregnant beyond the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the very old who have passed 60 years be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to bleed, in whatever way it is, it is necessary to clear the intestines with a gentle enema if they have much retained feces so that the veins do not draw harmful superfluities from the intestines into the principal limbs; one should not bleed those who are too full from meat, nor those who are drunk, as long as they remain so, or those who are suffering from dropsy. And one should not bleed after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, and excessive urination in women, or after exertion, watching all night, fasting, or any other activity that weakens the body, either from injury to the body or illness; then subtilize the humors if the blood is thick, through food and drink and medicine, if you have the skill. Then enter a bath if nothing impedes it, in order to subtilize the blood, and bleed from the vein on the foot around midnight, as we have said. And that day one should avoid exertion, and luxury, and similar things; and be calm and cheerful, and let the bleeder sit higher than the person being bled, and he should massage the arm two or three times, then tighten the ligature over it gently, for if it is too tight or too loose, it will not draw the blood. Then he should massage the area with his hands until the veins rise, and they can be felt; then he should moisten the blade of the bleeding knife with a little old oil, then place his left thumb on that vein below the site where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not withdraw from the knife.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flow like cords to the wound, and some are filled with windiness, so that when one puts fire upon it, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of those; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, for which reason the surgeon should be adept in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; if not, one must try again a little lower on that place or above, if the area isn't swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the wound is swollen and the patient is fearful, leave it for a day or two without binding the arm: perhaps hot abscesses will form; nor enter the bath, then begin the bleeding again if she pleases; and if the opening is small, let the blood flow gently through it and you doubt that as much blood does not issue as you wish, then apply the flame directly to that very opening; and work the wound gently, so that the limb becomes swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the vein swollen, do not re-bandage it but put a little linseed oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the linseed oil turns into fat; and so apply linseed oil to every bandage that you use for opening veins, to stop the flow of blood. And when applied to the wound, it acts subtly on the blood and disperses it when it is too abundant.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if large abscesses arise, which often happen, especially when the opening of the vein is small and the issue of blood is slight, then hasten and apply a sponge moistened with warm water to the wound, and hold it in place for an hour; and you should do this after the flow of blood from the vein has ceased. If any blackness or greenness remains in the wound afterwards, it does no harm; and if you see anything, apply some aloe or myrrh reduced to a pulp with rosewater, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and appearance of pus at the base of the thumb: therefore, put your hand on it, and if you feel softness with the pressure of your hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be sure not to place anything on the wound that we have mentioned, for it might enter the artery; but make a dry ointment to harden the area, then heal it with another healing remedy, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its blood flow and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if it appears thick, let it flow until it becomes thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and swollen, and needs bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and the incision should be wider; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and he should be bled little and often, and it must be bled by cutting diagonally, not puncturing; and this method of bleeding is safe from blood flowing and nerve damage, and is better than bleeding from a long or wide incision.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body needs bleeding, give moist bread in pomegranate juice; if he is heated, it should be given three or four times before the bleeding. And if his complexion is cold, eat moist bread dipped in syrup of myrrh, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and caraway, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after losing a lot of blood, then he should drink a broth made from meat, and a subtle scented syrup, and use the other things we mentioned in the section on syncope, for the opening of a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to open his arm and bleed again, he should do so little by little according to the amount of his continuing strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And those who want to open their arms after the first bleeding, and they have a strong body, should bleed .7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed elsewhere, they should bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is a lot of blood inside the body that has been heated and causes fever; so you must draw out a large quantity and widen the opening until it bleeds freely; then you should dress the wound as usual, and place your hand over his pulse while he heals, so that death does not come to him through the vein; this often happens when the surgeon is negligent. Also, when you see the arm loosening and the blood flowing out a second time, and the opening is closed, you must not press on it directly; nor if it is crooked, should you straighten the arm forcefully, for that would be harmful; instead, let him heal while his arm is relaxed; or you can touch the wound with the tip of a flame until the frozen blood at the vein's opening melts, then apply a little cold water and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not bind it, until the abscess is soothed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, let it be in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arms are healthy in the area of the vein in the head because it is composite.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of healing is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the vein turns red; then it should be let to drain slowly so that the vein appears clearly, then the wound should be bound tightly across, not from side to side or lengthwise; and the opening should be wide, and it should be bound close to the joint of the hand, and if it cannot drain, then put the hand back in hot water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is winter, do not re-immerse the hand in hot water, for it is more immersing than in the summer; and the healing of this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The healing of the salvation of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the method: straighten the hand and put it in hot water until the vein is swollen, as one can see; and if the vein is bound across, and you cover it completely from top to bottom, then there will be no harm; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are completely naked under the flesh. Then put the hand back in hot water if the blood has congealed in the wound and cannot drain.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have finished treating the blood as necessary, put oil and silk on the vein to seal it temporarily, and do the same for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of the soporific plant is good for all diseases beneath the body, such as diseases of the brain, and retention of fluids, and diseases of the kidneys, and of the hips and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its salve are such that the patient should soak their feet in hot water, and rub the salve onto the vein until it breaks, and apply it above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and running up the foot, treat the largest vein there, or at the ankle, whichever is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, then guard against the nerves that are underneath, and heal it across as well as up-and-down; and let the flames be anaesthetized.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot flow out, then immerse the foot in water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the salve fails on the first attempt, try again a little higher up, for the place is salty; do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and similarly prepare the other foot in the same way.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its pulsation relates to the pain in the hip when there is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of its salve are such that the patient should enter the bath, and twist their ankle IIII times, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it does open, treat it in all ways you can, and by crossing over; and it is better to cover it, for the place is safe, and it is very effective for many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not believe this, cut a vein in the leg, either in front or behind, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; and let blood flow until it stops, then loosen the bandage, and place cotton on it, and bind it tightly; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	from cupping marks
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or bronze, or glass; and cupping is performed according to two methods: either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is done by burning is performed in two ways: with or without fire; and cupping which is performed by burning and by bloodletting is carried out in 14 places on the body, one of which is on top of the head; another on the neck; two others on either side of the neck; a cup under the chin; cups on both shoulders; cups on the buttocks; cups on the upper arms; cups on the lower legs; and cups on the ankles. Cupping should not involve any bloodletting, except for small veins that are scattered throughout the body, so it does not weaken the patient in any way, as is done with bloodletting. It should also not be performed with or without fire in any disease that comes from repletion until the whole body has been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of sickness one must bleed, or due to habit, then we treat them every hour at the beginning of the month, or at its end, and in between, and at all times; for there are some who, when they need to bleed, have a heavy head; and there are those who experience bloating and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and there are those who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and vomit blood; and there are those who dream, and see through their eyelids things that are bad, and sad, and deadly, and similar.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially if it is during the month, we command them to fast after the third hour of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps with headaches ... that comes to the eyes, and should not be after the evacuation of the whole body; and this venting is in place of the bleeding of the head, and should not be used by those of a cold complexion, or who have catarrh, for it does them great harm; and because of this the old men should not use it, nor those with cold diseases in their heads.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal themselves frequently, become oblate, and because of this, one should place the leech lower down for fear of oblate.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation in the neck is located at the intersection of the windpipe and the basilic vein, and it helps to relieve pressure on the feet, and to open up the channels of the lungs, and to ease congestion and fullness; and it should be used sparingly, for if held too long, it will harm the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The second pair of ventilations in the neck help with headaches, eye pain and inflammation, strangulation, tooth pain, and they are located at the intersection of the basilic vein; instruct the surgeon to express his hand when placing them so that he does not press on the artery and cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The windings under the chin are good for mouth diseases, and gum decay, and similar diseases which are in the mouth; and it is in the sanctuary of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings on the shoulders are good for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilations in the armpits are like three veins in the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; instruct the surgeon to not go too deep, for underneath there is bare flesh, and beneath that are nerves and arteries.Li ventosation en la paume de la main si vaut a dolors et a repletion de la main et des doigtz, et est en leu de la sainie dou pis; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il ne cope mie l’artere.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass placed on the nape of the neck is useful for hemorrhoids and diseases below, and it should be a large cup made of copper, which it needs to effectively draw out blood; and if it were thin, it might break and cause large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping glasses on the legs heal very effectively, as they draw blood from the entire body, and are good for treating long-standing pains in the joints, the hips, and the bladder, and they relax the body in various conditions. They are placed at the .ij. sophenes, that is, the .ij. ankles, and yet they weaken the body after a long time, and bring on fainting in some people.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the suction cup is that you first place it empty, and gently suck, and apply it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the area become red and swollen, and the redness of blood appears; then let go, and re-apply the suction cups, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are those who have very thick skin and clear pores: one must strike only once, and one should make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to strike .ii times: the first time to open the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw blood a little at a time, we only need to strike once.Car li sans espés ne se traist pas en un coup, si est il necessaire de ferir la tierce fois.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we must suck repeatedly; and if the blood is thick, we pierce it with a needle, and the parts so that the heart be pierced suddenly, and it suits those who have thick and tough skin, and who have narrow pores, to anoint the places of the ventouses with an aperitif and dissolving oil: if it is in the summer, with violet oil, or with sweet almond oil, or with pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in the winter, with watercress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take oil of amarant, or of balsam, or dill oil, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one we heal has tender flesh and wide pores, no oil should be applied, but it must be washed after cupping with rosewater, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture, if they rise from parsley, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large swellings should drink old wine, or water from a spring, or a decoction of fennel or camomile, or similar things; and one should not bleed with leeches before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one should not sleep after being bled, and it is necessary that he be warm when he is to be bled and when he has been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And be wary if the person being bled is choleric, and if the blood is too thick and inflamed; then one should eat cold things like pomegranates, endive and lettuce with garlic, and similar things; and drink juices of plants, and charcoal from a fire, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold complexion should drink honey syrup, and moderate old wine mixed with young, and plant juices, and juices of small birds and squabs; and the day one is to be bled, one should drink more than eat; and it is good to give some men a little triacle or musk before or after bleeding to strengthen the main organs; and the blood must be thin but not for those with a hot temperament.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are placed without burning are those that are placed on the liver, and on the testicles, and on the gout, and on the belly, and on the buttocks, and on the thighs, and on the hips; for these members do not bear being burned under the eyes, and it is only done to draw blood from member to member, as we place them on the breasts when the nipples are healthy; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cupping glasses on the belly and buttocks to reduce the member; and it relieves pain when there is obstruction or stone, and by its attractive power it may draw out the obstruction or dislodge the stone from its place; and thus it acts when it is placed on the liver and on the testicles when there is retained flatulence, and these cupping glasses are administered empty merely to suck; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of the pleura, and in this way one fills the cupping glass with warm water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the fire cupping is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It is two fingers wide and a half palm deep, and it has a small hole around the middle for pushing in an awl, made of bronze, smooth at the front so that it does not bleed the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there is a crossbar of bronze or iron, to hold a candle, and they are large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who use them; for the ventouses used by children are different from those used by the elderly, and by the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And you must place this ventouse on the limb thus: take the candle of wax or the linen and place it inside the ventouse through the bar in the middle, so that the flame is at the bottom of the ventouse and does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, and hold your fingers over the hole we mentioned, so that when you want to, the vapour escapes, and remove the ventouse. Then take the linen as before and repeat frequently if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the glass cupping used for treatment of pleurisy, all types of acute diseases have no stem or opening, and are not relieved unless they are full of water, and are placed on the limb alone; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are not relieved unless in members where one cannot place cupping due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in bare flesh, such as toes or fingers, and others; and the quality of using them is that when you find leeches that are in clean sweet water without burrowing, then take them; and put one in sweet water, until they become accustomed and have nothing in their bellies; and then be bled from a vein and with cupping, then rub the member until it turns red, and place the leeches on it; and when they are full and bite, if it is a place where one can use cupping, then do so, for it is much better afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then raise the site with a pillow, and then with water, very gently, and then compress it; and if the bite marks are too close to the body of the leech, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place it over the bite, until the leech is suffocated; and if the bites are multiplied, place ground vitriol, or gall, and similar things, over the site, until they are suffocated; or place half a handful of peeled peas over the site, and leave them until they turn red around the bite, and it will then stop bleeding; and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches will not attach, then rub the bite mark with fresh blood, or stick a needle into it so that some blood comes out, and then place the leeches over it, and as soon as they smell the blood, they will attach; and when you see that they are defecating, then powder some ground aloe, or salt, or ash over them, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is a remedy for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish people who read this chapter will not find it in any of the ancient books, nor will they read any letters; and for this reason knowledge is strange in our land, for I have never found a good one; and I know nothing except through the science of the ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have acquired knowledge through them, and through experimentation, and by living a life of habit; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained within it, and have abbreviated it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say in the prologue of this book the sums of the matter and the chapters in which the sage places his understanding, and dwells upon their truth, so that those who have experience know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or fracture occurs in someone, you should hurry to heal the patient from both sides, if nothing else prevents it, such as weakness of the body, or old age; or if the weather is not very hot, or too cold; and eat cold foods, that is, cold joints, and deer and hare meat, and do not drink any wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have reason to suspect a hot abscess, or the discharge of matter from the limb; then return the patient to their previous treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the broken bone begins to heal, the patient should be nourished with foods that promote swelling or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testicles, pigs' feet, pig's belly, eggs, fresh fish, and full-bodied wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because with such nourishing the swelling will subside and the break will heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well healed or united according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but have no worry, reset the broken bone, the large tendons that stretch and join the limb together, as tightly as it was before; and do not stop at all in his work, and for this one should eat lots of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you should know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different than the fracture of the foot, or of the leg; and in this chapter I will tell you about all types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another that is only skin deep, like the cut of a quill pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture that is just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And in each way, there is its own method and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory comes to mind; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the limb is twisted, and it appears well from an external blow, and sounds when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twisting or pain on touch, and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no fracture; but there may be twisting, or splitting, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not advisable to move it by hand, but apply remedies that come later, and then hold it firmly but gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes into a tree, and the two parts are separated, they should now be brought together evenly, so that hot abscesses may come; and if cold abscesses come, then leave it for a day, until the abscess is healed; then put it equal to the movement that you can easily and gently, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restoration of that which has pieces; then hold it as it should be afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it is in two parts, whether it is a hand or a foot, or your hand if it is a small member, or at two strings, or at one string and your hand; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, then bring them back together by all means in their places as you can, and be careful that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient; and join the two heads of the bones well according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand if it doesn't seem right; then set it straight, but don't over-tighten or press too hard as those who cause hot abscesses and contractions in the limb by their treatment, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at its worst, then treat the patient carefully so that he does not move it, whether waking or sleeping, turning or in any other way; and be sure that the limb is secured so that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	Because when he feels no pain, then it is not at its worst, and you should put him in a good position so that he feels no pain; and be careful that he is placed straight, so that no crookedness comes to him when he is restored; and the qualities of the broken member are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs vary in size, shape, and appearance.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and hands and the like: these should be wrapped with soft, fine linen; and for larger ones, such as thighs and legs, use a broad, tough bandage, for broad bandages embrace the whole large limb and constrict it evenly all around, so that no swelling remains; then wind light bandages three or four times according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little at every turn of the bandage, then go over the broken part and tighten less, so that the fracture is moved away a little; then soften the bandage little by little, until you grasp a large part of the sound area, then take another bandage and wind it around straight again over the broken part; then go back to the part under the fracture and tighten gently, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we said in the first hour above; then place soft linen or bandages between the bandages, until they are all even, then bind everything on top with a bandage, and then place your splints well-fitted over it, if there is no abscess or swelling.
