Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put something hot on the abscess to reduce the swelling, and leave it for a few days; then stretch it over a wooden board, and let it be half the width of a broad cane, or a palm-branch, and let it be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but the board that is placed under the dislocation should be a little thicker and wider than the others; and it should be as long as the smallness or size of the limb requires; then stretch it over the boards as you did at the first stretching, and tie a string properly, as you did on the dislocation; the tighter it is, the better; and the strings should be medium-thin, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax; for if the strings are thick, as I have seen foolish people do, tying their bandages with cords of twisted flax, it is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too thin, and there should not be less than two fingers' width between each board.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is nervous because of the stars after the pressing in their healthy areas, then put under them flaxen lint or linen rags so that it does not hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should know that it is not advisable to manipulate all broken bones on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Because when the member is swollen, you should not put splints on it for more than five or seven days, or longer depending on the heat of the abscess; and here is the method of ancient plasters to heal fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that is kept on the walls of the mill, mix it with a lot of egg, and apply this preparation, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common way to use plaster to heal fractures in various conditions, especially in women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster to heal fractures and dislocations and twists: take 3 parts of lard and ladani and elecampane and assafetida and gum arabic and mastic, each at 10 parts; myrrh and aloe, each at 5 parts; and aloes, at 8 parts. Grind them to powder and mix with egg white; if the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it has a good composition and heals broken bones quickly, and it benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster that is good for twists: take myrrh and balsam, each 10 drams; mastic and aloe, each 9 drams; acacia gum 6 drams; Armenian bole 10 drams, and grind well, and mix with water or a lot of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of plaster for joints and bones separated from their places, and it eases the resulting pain, and treats the fracture: take new linen, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and apply it to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and it removes pain cleanly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that heals broken bones: take dry fig leaves and ground ivy leaves and grind them together to make a plaster.Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut as dislocation, et restoure le leu: pren mugat et vismalve, ana  .x.   ; mirre et aloes, ana  .viii.  ; acaice vi.  ; bolic armenic x.  , et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plaster to restore the fracture of the bone, and to reduce the remaining abscess: take new linen, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and apply it to the affected area.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of marshmallow, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, each one part; and grind them, and cook in wine, and if the member is scalded, cook it with moist coriander water, or water, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of plaster, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member.Take the juice of leeks and onions, and mix with vinegar, and apply it to the affected area until restored.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of viscum album, and the seed of flax, ballota, melilotus, and sansontia, and flowers of violets and chamomile, each one part; and crush, and cook in salted water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hyposurgeon writes in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb to heal it except for a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between soft and too hard.Et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs. Et s’il adveint qu’il soit trop sec, metez y oile; et s’il est trop moli, metez y cire; et si la brisure est grande, qu’on ne puet restorer, qu’on fasse cerote de cire et d’oile, et qu’on le broie tres fins, et qu’on y mette poudres d’armonie et de sante, et de violete, et qu’on le met sus la brisure, et qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen says that one should put on the broken limb, for healing, dry things that are slightly warm, such as myrrh, aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have said.Et dist galien qu’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit. Et s’il adveint que la brisure soit granz et profont, dist galien qu’on doit mettre sus la brisure cerote de cire et d’oile, et qu’on le broie tres fins, et qu’on y mette poudres d’armonie et de sante, et de violete, et qu’on le met sus la brisure.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of ointment that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and human hair, or bird feathers, and tallow, and mix them together, and grind them, and make an ointment out of it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, or that the bone has moved from its place; if not, loosen it by hand every few days. And if pain comes to the site, or itching, without rest or swelling, hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster immediately; and take a light cloth, and a sponge of sea-moistened, and dip into water, and lift the site until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed; then let the member rest for an hour, then place on wet linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and apply it to a nut, until you are sure of hot abscess; and let the inflammation of the affected member subside, and the pain be removed, then start the binding again subtly, and a little of the plaster, and do not pull it as tightly as before; and subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is closed and red and painful and swollen all over, and you need ointment and bandages, then resume it, just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the limb, do not dislodge it for three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it twenty days, according to what one sees, until the fracture is healed and the bone approaches the skin above; then restrain it more than before, and increase its meat as I have said before; and if you see the place drier than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come there; wet it therefore with warm water every time you dislodge it, and do this every third day, and loosen a little the bandage; thus nourishment comes to the limb by this work, and gently mend what the foolish doctor does, who restores the limb crookedly: this is bad practice, and it only causes wearying and doing it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various methods of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of fractures, with diverse appearances, and their causes differ. For there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and the neck bone is broken all the way to the sinew which is under the bone, as with an axe or a club; and this type of fracture is called "axe fracture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone without penetrating, and is called this type of fracture  "absolute"; and there are great or small wounds from these two fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a strike with the flat of the sword, or a cut, or from the collar bone, or from falling on stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture that penetrates, which approaches the membrane beneath the bone, or is on top of the bone; this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is in the bone as thin as a hair, and the crack is small, and because of this, such a fracture is called  "capillary"; and if the wound is made by stone or by falling, or in a similar way, and drives the bone piece inward, and the place is shaved like the blacksmiths when they work on kettles; then the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those who have moist bones in their heads, like the head of a child; and this happens with all types of fractures when small pieces are dislodged, as with tiles; I will speak about this later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by their deformity, and by the inquiry into the tent, and by the corruption of the flesh that is above it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is known because when the bone is uncovered and rubbed on top, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, pay attention to the accidents of the illness; and if you see no malicious accident, such as vomiting of phlegm, loss of consciousness, extension, paralysis, fever, eyes popping out and turning red, and other similar things in various dispositions, then it can heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no shocking accident, and you expect recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the baby comes to you first, and it is in winter, you should remove the foreskin before the fourteenth day when you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, you should hasten to remove the foreskin before the seventh day, so that the skin under the foreskin does not become corrupted, and so that the accidents we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes just to the membrane that covers the brain, then you should split the fractured part thus: and it is that you grasp the head of the wounded person, and expose the bone in every way you can, and over the wound more gently than you can, and if bleeding occurs when exposing the bone, or a swollen abscess, use the aid that is appropriate; and fill the area with moistened cloth in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the swollen abscesses are soothed, and be sure of the bleeding; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two ways of working: one way is that you saw closely in front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is to have various cuts, some narrow and some wide, with points, made of iron. Work gently so you do not hurt the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, you must pierce around it, so that you use cuts with chisels, not so deep that they go through the bone into the brain; and you must have a margin or circle above the point to prevent the tip from going through the bone. You should have several of these, so that each one comes in its turn to the thickness of the bone, and you should have chisels for all parts of the skull. And there are three ways to make these chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you place .i. probe on the bone and move your hand back and forth until you feel the bone is pierced; then move the probe elsewhere a little later, and do the same all around. Then cut into the space between the perforations with an incision, doing this as subtly and lightly as you can, as we have said, until you draw out the bone by hand or with one of your instruments, such as tongs or tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, it is appropriate that you remove the sharpness which is remained in the bone with any other similar instrument like a chisel, but it should be more slender and more subtle than the other chisel; and if anything of the small bones or scales remains, then remove them lightly with the instruments; then treat the wound as we have said with tenting and ointments.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is that which Galen describes, which is much safer; and he highly praises it, and his word is final.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must uncover a part of the bone where the fracture is open and moving. Once you have uncovered that part, place under it the cutting edge of this lens-shaped instrument, which is its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is sore on both sides, so that the incision is towards the bone; then tap with a small mallet, so that you gently hit the bone all around, and be careful of the membrane that is underneath; if it clings to the bone, loosen it gently, for the bone can be loosened without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture does not penetrate through to the membrane, and the bone is cut only slightly from above, with small pieces, then one must remove this roughness, and take away the scales with a very fine rasp of which you should have various sizes, in order to smooth each part according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use a large razor at first, and then a finer one afterwards, and do not stop doing this until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-cutting and subtlety techniques, you should apply it according to its purpose; and this is something that has not yet been answered for those who have dedicated their studies to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the sinus is exposed, you should take a piece of linen according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another piece of double linen, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first piece; and do this as gently as you can so that you do not burden the sinus, then administer a bandage on top, without tightening it more than is necessary to hold the wound; and leave it for one or two days, until the abscesses are relieved, then loosen it, and apply medicine such as roots of lilies, and flour of vetches, and incense powder, and aristologus, and similar things; and make a powder from these things, and place it on the wound, and apply mild medicines without biting; and ensure that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave any ointment, or allow any pus to gather, for when pus gathers on the membrane of the brain, it hardens and pierces, causing great harm to the patient; for when one applies something biting to the sinus, it heals from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care therefore, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, that it is without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness does not come except through the medicine that one has placed on it, how virtuous it is, then you should take a portion of honey and three parts of rose oil, and glue one piece of cloth, and place it on the ulcer; then heal it in ways that are appropriate, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose are broken, or one part alone, for they are two bones; and beneath is cartilage, which does not break but only bends or twists, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should boil your little finger or toe, and put the break inside your index finger or toe evenly, and in the pocket by force, until the nail returns according to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the fracture is above the nose, and the bones cannot be aligned, then you must place it evenly at the end of a rather thick thread.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, do this again, and try to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses are healed, then boil a tent of linen cloth at the tip of the nail, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you attach one to another part, if the fracture is there; and the tents should be so thick that they fill the holes in the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one must moisten the tents with butter, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that this is good, but one should moisten them in a mixture of egg white and mill dust; then leave the tent, as long as the bone is broken, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes they put in goose feathers instead of tents, and wrap around with a thin cloth, and keep the fracture still, and the patient breathes among them; now do what you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if hot abscesses come to the nose while you are working on it, then put cerate or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in a little diaquilon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes from it, then use a poultice of flour of sesame, and incense powder, cooked with egg white, then put over light gauze and do not bind it with anything; and if the fracture in the nail is small, and it is broken into small pieces, so remove it by means of suitable instruments for this, then clean the wound and heal it with healing ointments, and if there is no wound inside the nail, then cure it with tents and put splinters of black alder in it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of a broken jaw:
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken underneath and there is no open wound, and the break is only on the surface and not broken in two, one can know it easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right side, for you to put your right index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left jaw, then put your right index finger of the right hand, and put the fracture inside gently, and make it equal with the other hand by force.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is displaced in .ii., then you must administer an extension of .i. parts, so that it is equalized.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth, or chipping, then they must be restrained with a wire of gold, silver, or silk; then put cerotum on the broken jaw, and place a .i. double drape on it; and place upon the drape a large well-made splint, or a piece of leather equal in size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it onto the mouth as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the jaw is changing shape, then loosen it on the third day and then reset it to its original state; and place cerotum upon it again, of the powder from the mill with egg white or flour of sisament, after you have removed the previous cerotum; and place over the cerotum a light lining, and if the linings become sore, and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it takes to heal; many times it heals within 3 weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess comes, then administer what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine to see if any piece of bone has been dislodged; then remove it skillfully with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, dilate it with flame according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, then close the wound, if it is wide, and place upon it suitable poultices to promote healing.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks in several ways in front of the shoulder, and the break occurs in 3 ways: it can be broken and dislocated in two parts, which is the easiest to restore; or there can be a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is as follows when the break is without a wound: you need two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder where the forceps is broken; and the other extends the neck towards the affected part; then with your fingers, put the broken pieces back into alignment, so that the joint is in the correct position, with no misalignment or displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place a round pillow of cloth or linen underneath the shoulder, and make it as thick as necessary; then raise the forceps and hold the pillow in your hand, so that you put the broken pieces back into alignment, as they should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull out the head of the dislocated shoulder, because it comes up very tightly, then the patient should lie on his back, and put something under the shoulder, an ear, and the assistant pushes the shoulder down while pulling the arm upward, until the bone of the shoulder is dislodged.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then you must feel for the fracture with your fingers, and if it is stuck, then you must split it open; and gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined due to swelling, then apply this instrument under the shoulder to draw out the fluid.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It should have the shape of a spoon, and not be hollowed out, and be as wide as is appropriate according to the size of the bone and the extent of the work; and it should have two handles, as you can see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, according to the opening of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are certain about the hot abscess, cut open the wound, and if the opening is small, or if you doubt about a hot abscess, then close up the wound with bandages and tenting, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses appear, moisten a cloth in rose oil and garlic and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The dislocation of the bone, when there is no wound or fracture, is to place upon the bone the poultice made of mill-dust and egg white, and put light sponges on top, and place a sphere underneath the axilla, if you need it; then take a very broad band, one palm wide, then place a folded cloth on top of the sponges and the poultice; then take a slender staff, three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the band so that the head of the band hangs down; and place the staff upon the fracture, and wind the band around the neck, and underneath the sound axilla, and under the injured axilla; and adjust it from each side, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the staff does not move on top of the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the ligature loosens, then restrain it; and let the patient lie on his back, and when he sleeps, put a small pillow underneath the axilla to raise the shoulder; thus the fracture will be lightened by the strengthening of the shoulder joint, or you can bind his arm to his neck, and do not release him if an evil accident does not occur, up to twenty days; then recommence the poultice, if you see that he needs it, and adjust it thus, until he is healed; and he is usually healed within 28 days, but some men heal more quickly.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Then it happens that the shoulder is broken or dislocated in a large place or in the middle, and one does not feel it except by touch; then apply the apparatus according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way you can; then put flour from the mill with an abundance of eggs over the site, and light compresses, and place a double cloth over that; then place a broad, thin board over it, a little wider than the shoulder, and if there is any swelling underneath the board on the shoulder, fill that indentation with compresses of linen so that the board lies flat; then tighten it with a large bandage firmly so that the board does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and every time it loosens, tighten it again, and adjust the board if it has moved out of place, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number of days is complete, loosen it, and be careful, for it is not a bone that sets easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone protrudes forward, and not beneath the heart, they should push it up, and the bone, and do as we said in the breaking of the forceps to soothe the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The leg is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; it often breaks at the knee.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends downward, and the patient feels great pain and weakness throughout his body, and sometimes vomits blood, and there are open wounds in the broken bone, which he feels with his fingers.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that the patient lies on his back, and places a cushion between his shoulders, then presses his shoulders together, and joins the ribs with his hands, ensuring that the bone is set correctly in all ways; then applies plasters and bandages over the wound below, using a subtle mixture of salt or other light substance, and wraps it in a cloth, placing it over the broken bone so that it does not move; then he winds the bandage around the body, and tightens it gently, and checks every hour if it has loosened, and if it has, he tightens it; and if it needs to be removed due to corrosion or itching or pain or abscess, he should hurry and remove it, cleaning what has come from the wound in various ways of treatment; then he reapplies the plaster and tightens it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that rib fractures only occur in the large ones near the back, and in the chest near the head, and they only bend because they are slippery; and one can tell [this] well through examination of the two sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is to set the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the ointment, and bind it with a cloth, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is declining towards the interior, then the patient feels great pain and stabbing, as with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; and also has a cough, and coughs up a large quantity of blood, and it is a serious illness, and the ancients placed great importance on it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that one should administer foods that swell the belly, to push the fracture out.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, unless hot abscesses come to it, if they have not come to it already.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come to it, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one should put cupping glasses on the area to draw out the excess fluids, and this is reasonable; however, there is a risk that the cupping glass will attract the excess fluids due to the weakness of the body.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the area with soft lamb's wool soaked in hot oil, and place a tent between the ribs to ensure even pressure all around, then it should be bandaged with bandages of pleurisy, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain where the bone breaks through the bandage, and there is doubt about the patient, then one should cut above the broken rib, and place an instrument to ward off the saphena vein; then one must split the bone, and gently pull it out, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with ointments until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a painful abscess comes, place wet cloth in rose oil, and apply it to the affected area; and treat the area around the abscess as needed, and let the patient lie on their side where it is, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	from the fracture of the neck:
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a fracture in the bones of the neck, and it can be bent; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover or not, take note if their hands are soft and swollen and numb, and they cannot move or straighten them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is deadly in many ways, and if they are numb and feel pain when you stretch or pinch them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the illness is healed, if proper care is given.And si li mains ne sont pas mollifiiez ne enflees ne mortes, et les sent bien quant on les estraint, sache que li maux est de la chair ou de la peau et qu’il n’est pas de l’os; et si tu le mets en cure, il sera sain.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar condition occurs in the spine of the back, and you want to know whether it is healthy or not, then take note if the feet are swollen, and if the symptoms are present which are in the hands, and in the back there is flatulence and defecation without volition; and when he has been placed on his stomach, there is also defecation without volition.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is placed on his back and he wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal; do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these effects do not occur, then the condition is less severe.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is an abscess, apply warm rose oil or hen's egg oil to the spine until it is soothed; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bandage it with a linen cloth; and command the patient to rest, and not sleep on the painful side until he is cured.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, you should cover it with the heart; and take out the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a stitch, then treat the wound with ointment mixed with chalk, until it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the 'head of the cow', fill your poultice-bag with your left hand, and place it equally in your other hand at your will, then apply the plaster and the bandage on top of it, if you need to; then tie it tightly, and if there is a bone dislocated, do the same, take it out, and treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It sometimes happens that the hip bone is fractured, and if it does, there will be a slight depression at the head; and they feel long and inclined to one side, and the patient feels pain in the area, and there is tenderness and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And its restoration is that you extend your hand over it, so that you are on the break; and know which is the upper and lower part of the fracture; and if the fracture is only at the head, then place that fracture evenly, so that it is in its natural shape.Et se ele est au bas, si doit estre sous, et se ele est a l’un costé, si doit estre sous, et ne doit pas estre sur le chief, tant qu’ele soit sanée; car celi qui sont desous doivent estrendre cele qui sont sus, et non pas contrer.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	If the fracture is long, or if it slopes downward, have the patient lie on his stomach until the healing of that fracture is prepared for.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it straight, put on the poultice, then put on a splint of wood or of horn, and hold the fracture so that it does not move; and apply the bandage below the ribs, until the limb is set straight.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if painful bumps arise, do not touch them until the painful bumps are soothed, and apply what we have mentioned before; then return to the healing, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad occurrence; and that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoires is that which is between the neck and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one should restore it according to either of two methods; one of which is to take a rod of medium thickness, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Tie the two ends with cords and raise them up high, and have the patient sit on a seat; then let him hang his broken arm over the rod, until it comes to rest, and hold in place with a bend in the rod; then have him lie down on something heavy so that another person can stretch the arm downward; then have the helper place the dislocation back into alignment with their hands together, until it is as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is to have the patient lean on his elbow, and tie his hand to his neck; then have one minister hold what is above the dislocation in their hands, and the other minister hold beneath the dislocation, at each end of the rod, and stretch each end in opposite directions.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you want the extraction to be more thorough, then tighten the ligature below the fracture, and above it as well, and each assistant must do their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, then you should place one ligature in the middle below the joint, and another towards the neck, under the fracture; and likewise, if the fracture is towards the neck, then a light ligature should be placed gently, without exertion, so that the fracture remains even on the joint, and above the neck; then make the fracture even as it should be, and tighten it, if no abscesses form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if warm abscesses come, then do not compress it until the 7th day, and put soft lamb's wool in oil of roses on the warm abscesses, until they are relieved; then compress, and the way to compress is that you put the plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm above the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the bandage, and compress on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in place of stars, if nothing deflects it, or if the bone is not displaced.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is displaced, then use stars, and put a larger and stronger star on the fracture, and have between each star 1 finger of space, and let each star be as large that it passes the fracture by 3 fingers on each side; then compress over the stars, thus as I said at the beginning of the chapter, over the fracture, more strongly and less by moving away.Et si li briseure est vers le coute, si covient que tu mettes la main sus l’espaule, et l’autre main sus lou col, et use d’esteles plus forts sus lou bras, et sus l’ajutoire, ou se li os est brisez; puis estrain sus les esteles, en alant devers le chief, et que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the stars, and the tightening, as we have said, at the time that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the hot abscess, let it be bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine the ligature every three days, so that itching or swelling does not come to the site, or the growth of the infection may not come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the abscess, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, do not loosen the ligature until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and place under the shoulder a pillow filled with wool of equal thickness, and examine every hour during the day or night that the figure of the broken member does not move, or the ligature become softened; then let the abscess heal by the power of medicine, and give him the food that we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is most subtle at first; and when he begins to recover, let the food be thicker.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be bound for forty days all around, and then one must release them and administer baths and ointment medicines to direct the place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the dislocation is severe and stuck, it remains to be released for 50 days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the 'ulna', one of which is small, and it follows the armpit; and the other is large, and it is located under the little finger towards the hand; sometimes only the large ulna breaks, or the small one, and sometimes both.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, their restoration is easier and healing faster; but when the larger ones are broken, healing is more difficult and painful than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only a small bone that is broken, then one must extend it slightly and put it in place.And if a large bone is broken, one should not extend it too much, but put it in its place with a little extension.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is a large bone, one should apply greater force to it; and let him lie on his back, and let the wounded arm be higher than the other, and the little finger lower than all the others, and let the patient cross himself over himself, and let there be a pillow in front of him so that he feels no pain; then let one minister extend his upper arm towards his hand, or to the elbow, and another minister above that.And let them hold it tightly for a little while until they feel the bone enter its place; then they must release it immediately and put on the poultice quickly.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the bandages on evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the bone has broken into pieces, place each one in its proper position; and if any have become dislocated, and you cannot restore them to their places, then cut through the bone, as we have described earlier.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it specifically in this chapter; so take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the treatment hot abscesses appear, glue a bandage of cerate made of rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and then gently lay the bandage on top, so that the hot abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerate, and apply the plaster made from mill-powder with an egg, and then put on the bandages, and let the bandage over the fracture be a bit stronger, and a little larger than the others; and you should have six bandages on the arm in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and tighten more over the fracture than elsewhere, and at all times less as it heals, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages over the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread by which it is tightened be made of flax, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And re-examine the limb and the joint after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you should wet the limb with warm water until the itch is relieved; and let the limb not be tightly bound but at rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then renew the binding, and if the ligaments are relaxed and the bones dislocated, and similar things, then correct it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if one must guard against the nutrients not being able to reach the member because it is too bound up, then one must loosen it a little and leave it thus for some days, until the nutrients flow to it, and then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said happens to the patient, then do not loosen it for 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or if he can move his neck without pain, then he may use his hands to support his neck, and keep his neck straight, and guard against movement and effort, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is healed in 30 or 35 days, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and on the fingers there are few fractures, and they only come from many foldings.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or folded, then the patient should bend his hand, and keep it straight in front of him evenly; then he should put his hand on the stretched cloth, and stretch the broken bones, and put them together evenly, and then apply the plaster and poultices, if there are no abscesses, and then put on a splint according to the amount of the break; and let it be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the peritoneum around the abdomen of the plant, make a sponge, and instruct the patient to squeeze it at the site of the broken plant; then squeeze it with a long strip of cloth, and let the mark of the burn be as large as the palm of the hand, and squeeze it as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the forearm, you must put a splint on top and another underneath the plant, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture is in any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, put it in a cast, as it should be; and squeeze it with the palm, and see if you put a small straight splint to raise the fracture, and do not move it; and if the fracture is in one of the other fingers, like the index finger or one of the others, put it in a cast, and bind it with the healthy finger that is next to it; either tie them all together while holding them, or put a splint on top, as in the thumb; take care with the healing and the preparation of a hot abscess, and treat any pus that comes out, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The thighbone is often broken, and one can see it well when it turns forward and backward; its restoration is by binding with a ligature above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each assistant stretches their band to their side equally; and this is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, let one ligature be towards the armpit, and the other ligatures below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is close to the knee, then let the ligature be beyond the knee, and let the extension be below; then put the mirror to the bone equal to its natural shape with his two hands, until it is level, and then apply the poultice and the bandage, and if no abscess forms.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside first and then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is done in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap the fracture with a long bandage doubled in two or three layers, and leave the excess, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the buttock, and tie the long thread between the thigh and the leg beyond the knee below, and let the ends of the thread come above; then go up the leg and the thigh with the bandage, then put splints on the fracture, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then tighten the space between the leg and the thigh with soft rags to make it equal, then start to tie three turns or four above the fracture; and the more you go above the fracture, the less you tighten; then grasp the two ends of the thread that you have tied between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then go back below to the end of the thread, so that you come under the foot; and tighten it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, so that no abscess or swelling or other similar thing comes.
